However, if the Municipal Government Auditorium could not be used, the National Goods Association would not have enough funds to build a shed for the entertainment show. He also proposed seeking ways to use airplanes to distribute National Goods leaflets. (B) Discussion Items: (1) Re-discuss the budget for the inauguration ceremony. Decision: Reduce the budgets of each group to about 10,000 yuan and resubmit for approval. (2) Determine the time for the inauguration ceremony and various reviews. Decision: Review of troops at 8 AM, inauguration ceremony at 10 AM, Boy Scout review at 11 AM, and National Goods Association held at the same time. Review of the Fire Brigade at 2 PM. Submit to the Mayor for approval. (3) Submit to the Mayor a request for the China Eurasia Aviation Corporation to distribute National Goods leaflets in the city center. Decision: Passed. (4) Submit to the Mayor a request to the China Aviation Association to transfer to the Aviation Administration to send aircraft purchased by various sectors of the city to perform in the city center. Decision: Passed. (5) Decide on the date of the next meeting. Decision: Next Tuesday at 3 PM in the Municipal Government Auditorium.

Seafarer Certification Examination 150

Will be Held in Beijing as Scheduled

A telegram from Nanjing states that the Shanghai Merchant Ship Drivers Association has requested to extend the period for the seafarer certification examination and move it to Shanghai. The Ministry believed that the reasons stated were not without merit and should be considered for future adoption. However, this certification examination is not a widespread event and has already been notified to the seafarers who are required to take the examination. It is not appropriate to change it, so it has been decided to hold the examination in Beijing as scheduled.

A Record of the Typhoon and Flood Disaster in Chuansha and Nanhui 151

On September 2nd, a hurricane passed through Shanghai, and the seawalls in the coastal areas of Chuansha and Nanhui counties in Pudong were mostly destroyed. Fields and houses near the sea were almost completely washed away. The most severely affected areas were Hengsha, Neigaodun Township, Xinsha Township, and Yuanyuansha in Chuansha. There were refugees everywhere, sleeping in the open and eating in the wind. Local officials and gentry were urgently repairing and providing relief, but their efforts were a drop in the bucket. Realizing the severity of the disaster, our newspaper specially sent Li Zunyong to take photographs, and Shen Zijian, in his capacity as a member of the Pudong Fellow-Villagers Association, went to survey the disaster. They agreed to travel together. When they arrived at Laogang, which belongs to Nanhui County, they encountered the second typhoon and flood on the 18th. Seeing the disaster situation, they felt even more saddened. Now, we have organized the diary and written a survey report, along with seventeen early photographs. From our newspaper, we went to Dongjiadu, took the Southbound bus to Zhoupu, and transferred to a small vehicle. It was a Sunday, and passengers with party membership and teachers wearing party badges were exempt from fares. At 6 PM, we arrived at Nanhui. We visited County Magistrate Yuan, who explained the current situation in the disaster area and the route of the inspection in detail. He also summoned Yang, the First District Chief of Nanhui, to the office to report on the disaster situation. We also visited Xu Shinai, who said that this time, the sea tide was fortunately a northeast wind, so the submerged areas were flooded with fresh Yangtze River water. If it had been a southeast wind and the floodwater was salty, not only would there be no hope for the autumn harvest, but it would probably not be possible to cultivate the land for two or three years. That night, we stayed in a hotel. At 10 AM the next morning, we went to Laogang. When we set off, there was already wind and rain. The boat was small, and Zijian and Li huddled in the cabin. When we arrived at Laogang Town in Wanggongtang, our clothes were soaked. We changed to a rowboat and went to Ligongtang, which is the port of Laogang. We saw that the cotton, soybeans, sweet potatoes, and other crops planted in the fields were submerged in water. There was a coffin, of unknown origin, floating by, and no one cared about it. (With photograph) At that time, the northeast wind was howling, and the rain was pouring. The farmers in Ligongtang, mindful of the ferocity of the first typhoon and flood, were fleeing in groups. (With photograph)

(Floating Coffin, Photographed by Li Zunyong) 152

While in the rowboat, Zijian's umbrella was broken by the wind. (With photograph) Climbing up Ligongtang, he was almost blown over. Unable to withstand the wind, he abandoned the umbrella and stood on the embankment. Looking into the distance at the collapsed embankments north of Laogang, he saw farmers in the remaining thatched huts carrying their belongings and fleeing to Wanggongtang. Ligongtang is near the sea and about four li from Wanggongtang. He had visited the embankment construction project in previous years. Seeing the port of Laogang, it was different from before. He asked the locals, who said that Ligongtang had collapsed several times, receding dozens of zhang.

The rivers between Wanggongtang and Ligongtang were crisscrossed and evenly spaced, looking like the Chinese character 田. The riverbanks were very low, only about a foot above the water surface, making it easy for them to be flooded during high tide. After the hurricane on September 2nd destroyed the seawalls, the cotton, soybeans, and other crops planted in the fields were submerged in water for three to five days. Some of the plants had mud clinging to their leaves, and the entire plants died. But many of the crops still had one or two chances of survival. This month, however, they were hit by a second typhoon and flood, completely destroying them. According to the town chief, more than 250 corpses and more than 1,300 people, big and small, were in the affected area.

The farmers outside Wanggongtang are from Tongzhou and Haimen, while the farmers inside the embankment are mostly from Chongming. They have lived inside for decades. The farmers inside and outside the embankment are all tenant farmers. The landlords, in addition to Widow Relief, Infant Nurturing, and Universal Relief Halls, are all local landowners. The rent ranges from five yuan to five jiao.

Zijian stood on Ligongtang, almost blown away by the strong wind and rain, and went to the foot of the embankment. He entered a farmer's house, where the chicken coop was under the table and the pigsty was connected to the bed. People and animals lived together. But to avoid the wind and rain, it seemed like a mansion. Li braved the rain to photograph the collapsed embankment. (With photograph) It was said that the collapsed embankment stretched for more than 200 zhang from Laogang to Erzaohong. We returned to Laogang Town in a rowboat, changed clothes at the inn, which was just a low house made of reed mats and plastered with lime. The rain leaked through the roof. We originally planned to start from Laogang Town and go north to Wutuan and Chuansha. The inn had a south-facing window with glass, and looking out at the wind and rain made people shudder. The merchants in the town said that with this wind, the sea tide would probably be even worse than the previous one. They were all planning to evacuate. The people on the street all covered their heads with burlap sacks. The innkeeper was an old woman. (With photograph) Knowing that we had come to survey the disaster, she treated us cordially, drying our wet clothes and serving hot tea. She said that transportation in Laogang Town was extremely inconvenient when it rained. So Li and I decided to take the original boat back to Nanhui. The wind and rain were even heavier on the way. When we arrived in the city, it was already 7 PM. We still stayed in the hotel, and all our clothes were wet. We wrapped ourselves in a woolen blanket, and the lamp flickered on and off until it went out completely at 11 PM. That night, there was a strong wind and rain, and some walls in the city collapsed. Outside the West Gate, a female worker was blown into the river while holding an umbrella and drowned. On the 19th, the Nanhui Land Passenger Wheel, all suspended operation. At 9:30 AM, the Chuansha Passenger Wheel, came from Sandun, through here. Since Li's clothes were completely wet and he had caught a cold the day before, he could not go. In the afternoon, the wind and rain eased slightly, and we visited Xiangguang Tower, where Dong Qichang studied. (With photograph) That day, we were staying in the Anju Hotel, and we heard that Laogang Town had been submerged. The inn where we had planned to stay the night before was already in the water. On the 20th, County Magistrate Yuan sent Director Ling to accompany us to Wutuan. We took a boat to Zhuqiao Town, and the Public Security Bureau sent police officers and police to escort us. (With photograph) We surveyed from Panjia Hong to Wangjia Hong, belonging to Wutuan and Liutuan. That section of Ligongtang had not been destroyed, but one-tenth of the shore shed outside the embankment (i.e., the weir built by the businesses) was destroyed. Farmers were afraid and slept in the open on the embankment. (With photograph) When we were at Panjia Hong, some farmers heard that we had arrived and came in groups to ask for food, kneeling on the ground and pulling us so that we could not move. We were saddened by this, and the police officers persuaded them kindly before they let us go. (With photograph) We walked on the weirs that had not been destroyed, for about a mile, and locusts flew around us and attached themselves to our bodies. The weirs in Qiujia Road in Liutuan were not destroyed, but the weirs in Nijia Road, Shijia Road, and Zhangjia Road were all destroyed. At Majia Road, there was a large fishing boat stranded at the foot of Ligongtang. When asked how it got there, they said that it was washed in by the tide and could not be moved. Walking north along Ligongtang, we only saw disaster victims on the embankment, setting up bamboo and wooden shelters for lodging, and hanging wet clothes and quilts on bamboo poles to dry. From a distance, it looked like a market or temple fair in the north. Downslope of the embankment, there were piles of messy rice straw, broken tables, wooden beds, pots and stoves, and broken wood and bamboo, etc., for 30 or 40 miles along Ligongtang, with no place untouched, which were floating homes, blown by the northeast wind, parked at the bottom of the embankment. When farmers look for their possessions and cannot identify them, there are often disputes. By the time we surveyed Qituan, it was late, so we went to Jiangjia Road. The police officers and police returned to Zhuqiao, and we and Director Ling went to Chuansha to visit County Magistrate Li. County Magistrate Li had just returned from surveying the weirs in Batuan and Jiutuan. We talked in the office. His secretary, Mr. Shen, was the son of Shen Yugang and He Jing, who was an old friend of us. That night, we stayed at Zhiyuan Hall.

On the 21st, we surveyed from Changtang in Chuansha and saw that the slope of Ligongtang was planted with locust trees. (With photograph) And the Ligongtang in the boundary of Nanhui did not have this protection. We asked, and it was planted by the Chuansha Farm. The fields below the embankment belonged to the Chuansha County Education Bureau. The disaster situation outside the embankment was no different from that of Liutuan and Qituan. When we arrived at Sanjiagang, we saw three tile houses that had not collapsed. (With photograph) Looking at their foundations, they were filled about four feet higher than the ground. During the high tide, water entered the house and did not submerge the walls. Thus, we knew that all the thatched houses outside the embankment from Wutuan to Qituan to Shisantuan that had not collapsed also had higher foundations. When we arrived at Liujia in Batuan, a man named Zhao Xiaogou and his entire family of five were crushed to death by a washed-away house, and the head embankment was destroyed. (With photograph) Li's photographic materials were used up, so he took the Shangchuan bus from Bailongjiang to Xiaowan and returned to the newspaper.

Early on the 22nd, we took the Shangchuan bus from Xiaowan to Bailongjiang, took the patrol boat of the Chuansha County Government, and crossed Hengsha. Before entering the harbor, we saw a corpse floating in the sea. At 3 PM, we arrived at the Sixth District Office in Wenyu Town. We were accompanied by the local Public Security Bureau chief to inspect the old weir. We saw a woman, about twenty years old, arranging wet clothes on the Shencang weir. When asked her name, she seemed shy and refused to answer. An older woman, about fifty years old, came out from a reed mat next to her, answering politely. We knew that she was a member of some family, from the upper class, still living in the open. We could know the rest by analogy. There were Chen Xie and his shop giving porridge in Wenyu South Street, and dozens of people came to eat. (With photograph) Hengsha suffered even more severely due to its geography. It was beyond the power of my clumsy pen to describe. That night, we stayed at the District Office.

Nanhui and Chuansha face the sea on the east. Outside, there are Qinchanggong Tang, Wanggong Tang, and Ligong Tang, which protect the embankment and are all in a straight line. Outside Ligong Tang, there are still people's weirs. What was destroyed was only more than 200 characters of Ligong Tang and the people's weirs in each group. Hengsha is isolated in the sea, facing the sea on all sides. The owners enclose weirs on the ground, summon tenants, and collect rent. The tenants are also from Chonghai. The rent ranges from five yuan to 36 cents.

Early on the 23rd, we departed from the District Office and surveyed from Wanzhi Township to Houde Township and Wengqing Township. We saw that the uncollapsed houses were completely submerged in water. People traveled back and forth with round wooden tubs or bamboo rafts. (With photograph) The carcasses of dead livestock still had a lot of stench. Each township has weirs with weir workers, which are called weir cuts in the Hengsha dialect. We traveled to the weir cuts, and the farmers fought to carry us on their backs. A man named Xuelang followed us for several miles, carrying us three times. Dear compatriots, suffering such a catastrophe, how can we not be moved by compassion?

We returned from Houde Township and arrived at Gaodun Township, when we heard a loud gong. The Public Security Bureau chief who was traveling with us sent police to inquire and learned that they wanted to ask for exemption from land rent. We told them that we were busy with emergency relief these days, so how could we have rent? Fearing that they were taking the opportunity to incite unrest, we ordered them to be taken to the District Office, and they were released that night. When we arrived at Gaodun Weir, we encountered two French priests who were also inspecting and providing relief. (With photograph) We rested in the warehouse of the Education Public Group in Fengle Town. The farmers heard that we had arrived and came in groups to request emergency relief. People without clothes, food, or shelter could not last long with only three or four days of grain. The people who traveled with us told them that the Chuansha County Government had allocated 200 shi of relief rice, 100 of which were purchased and transported from Shanghai and would arrive within two days. We also pointed to us and said that the Pudong Fellow-Villagers Association had sent us to inspect and that the great philanthropists of Shanghai had contacted various organizations to raise relief funds, hoping that everyone would temporarily be quiet and not be agitated. First, the warehouse of the Education Public Group had selected tenants to repair the weir as a form of work-for-relief and urged them to work quickly and not rely solely on relief grain. The farmers gradually dispersed. That night, we stayed in the warehouse. (Note: Due to space limitations, we could not publish all of the above organizations.) On the morning of the 24th, we hired a sampan and originally planned to detour around Yuanyuansha and enter the Wusong Estuary. It happened to be a southeast wind, so we thought that the journey would be quick. Unexpectedly, when we exited, it was very difficult to steer the boat because it was large and the port was small, costing about an hour. When we arrived at the east of Yuanyuansha, we calculated the journey. If we lingered in Yuanyuansha, we would have to wait for the tide outside the Wusong Estuary tonight. Our companions advised us not to go ashore, saying that the disaster situation in Yuanyuansha had been reported to the Chuansha County Government and that the situation was similar to that of Hengsha. We had no choice but to look at the beach from a distance and saw only one or two thatched sheds. When we arrived outside the Wusong Estuary, we saw that the stone embankment on the west beach had also been destroyed. We took the Shanghai-Nanjing train and saw that the cotton and rice in the Wusong area were also submerged in water. We arrived at the newspaper at 7 PM.

Ambiguity in the Execution of Successfully Mediated Cases 155

The Judicial Yuan Clearly Explains the Instruction Received by the Municipal Government

The Municipal Government yesterday issued an instruction from the Executive Yuan, stating: "It is found that the Ministry of Interior has previously submitted a report stating that the Civil Affairs Department of Zhejiang has submitted a report requesting an explanation of the ambiguities in the execution of cases successfully mediated by the district, township, and town mediation committees. The report was forwarded to the Judicial Yuan for explanation. The Ministry of Judicial Administration also submitted its opinion on the case, requesting consideration and implementation. The case was then merged and forwarded to the Judicial Yuan for explanation. Now, we have received Advisory Letter No. 961 from the Judicial Yuan, stating that the Legal Interpretation Meeting of the Court has resolved that civil cases that have been legally mediated by the court before litigation have the same effect as a final judgment, as stipulated in Article 15 of the Civil Mediation Law. In accordance with Article 4 of the Civil Procedure Execution Rules, compulsory execution can be enforced. As for the mediation conducted by district, township, and town mediation committees, since there is no clear stipulation that it can be used as a basis for execution, if one party does not comply with the mediation agreement, in addition to filing a lawsuit with the local court to confirm the establishment of the mediation and ordering payment, execution may not be requested." In light of this, in addition to issuing separate orders, the original reports of the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Judicial Administration are hereby copied and issued, so that you may be informed and instruct your subordinates to be informed. This order is attached, briefly.

A Humorous Episode of a Bride Eloping 165

Twice the Car Arrived but She Refused to Come; The Old Man was Ashamed and Angry and Even Wanted to Throw Himself into the River

The Groom Sees the Father-in-Law to Negotiate Extensively; Intensifying the Search and Temporarily Not Litigating

Shu Fanglai of Yangzhou, living above the Luoyang Shoe Store on the Bund, French Concession, has a son named Kaike, who is 24 years old. Since childhood, Shu Fangzhang relied on four matchmakers who were friends, Wang Zhengkun, Mrs. Shu Zhai, Mrs. Wang Xie, and An You, to betroth to him Ji Juyuan's daughter, Xiaolianzi (now 17 years old), from the same village, as his daughter-in-law. Over the past week, both parents, because Kaike and Xiaolianzi have both come of age, are suitable for marriage, so the original matchmaker, Wang Zhengkun, and others, travelled between the two families to discuss the bride price, totaling 160 yuan. However, Shu has always been a shoemaker and lacks savings at home. How could he come up with such a large amount of silver at once? Although he tried his best to ask his relatives and friends for help, he still failed to collect the money. Therefore, he asked the matchmaker Hu to go to the bride's home again to explain that the previously agreed bride price of 160 yuan should be cancelled, but the bride's clothes and ornaments, and all the equipment in the new room, should be prepared by the groom's family, so the bride's family need not prepare a dowry. Ji also agreed at the time, and then chose the 24th of this month to hold the wedding. However, Ji's daughter, Xiaolianzi, because the groom's family still wanted to temporarily change the agreed bride price of only 160 yuan and could not come up with it, which showed how poor the family was, and thinking that after she married into the family in the future, her daily life would be unimaginable, she asked her father to carry out the cancellation of the marriage. However, Ji refused because this matter was related to his reputation. Seeing that her father did not agree, Xiaolianzi was unhappy all day long. In the blink of an eye, the auspicious day (the day before yesterday) had arrived. Because Shu's house was small, he rented the Dahonglou Restaurant on Wuma Road, hanging lanterns and decorations, and making great preparations. Guests filled the door, and it was very lively. When it was time for the wedding in the evening, Shu sent a car he had prepared to the bride's house at No. 7 Youche Wharf, Nanshi, to pick up the bride. Unexpectedly, even after going twice, the bride was not brought back. All the guests were greatly suspicious, and there was much discussion. Shu, because his face had been completely lost, wanted to throw himself into the Pubin River to commit suicide. After the groom Kaike and others repeatedly persuaded him, he stopped. On one hand, he immediately forced the original matchmaker Zheng Kun to go straight to the bride's house by car at about 2 a.m. yesterday morning to question his father-in-law Ji Juyuan and ask where the bride had gone and why she refused to get into the car (the wedding car). At this point, Ji had to apologize again and again, and explained that Xiaolianzi had privately escaped last night (the 23rd). Even now, although he had searched everywhere, there was still no trace of her. When the new groom heard this, he thought that the bride's family intended to renege on the marriage, and grabbed his father-in-law, demanding to hand him over to the police officer Tian Xiaoquan of the 25th Precinct. The police officer then brought him to the First District, First Precinct, where the director preliminarily interrogated him. Shu Kaike suddenly agreed to his father-in-law's request, giving him a period of time to intensify the search. As soon as the girl was found, he would immediately send her to his home, so he did not want to litigate anymore. The director, because both parties did not pursue the matter further, ordered them to leave the precinct and resolve the matter amicably. A humorous episode of a bride eloping thus came to a temporary end.

Cui Laosan Died of Anger After Being Slapped in the Face by a Woman 166

A Stinking Negotiation Led to a Death; An Arrest Warrant Issued and the Woman Commited a Great Disaster

Cui Laosan, a Chongming native, 45 years old, lived at No. 22, Bao'an Division Road, Hujia Muqiao, Hongkou. A tenant, A'er, lived in his house. A'er was a night soil collector. At about 2 p.m. the day before yesterday, he went out to dump the night soil. The night soil cart was parked in front of the iron shop opened by Chen Yang, and the foul smell spread everywhere, directly hitting people's noses. Chen was furious and ordered the cart to leave. A conflict broke out between the two sides. Cui Laosan passed by and tried to mediate, but Chen continued to roar. Cui then said that there was no need to argue with this shrew, and to wait for her husband to return home to settle the score. Chen thought that Cui's words were disrespectful, so she stepped forward and slapped Cui Laosan in the face. Cui suffered this great humiliation. In his mind, a man slapped in the face by a woman was extremely unlucky. He refused to let the matter rest. Neighbors mediated, and Cui went home with his head lowered. He immediately collapsed on the bed. Unexpectedly, at about 8 p.m., Cui Laosan died of anger. His family reported that he had died from being beaten, so they reported to the Third Precinct of the Fifth District and had Chen arrested. Yesterday, they ordered the Baodi Li A'er to report to the Temple Court for an autopsy.

Xu Qizhong's Dispute with a Dancing Girl over Cohabitation 167

They Initially Entered an Agreement to Live Together Intimately

But Suddenly Abandoned Her as if She Was a Stranger

Chen Hailun Came to the Door to Demand Alimony

She Was Grabbed and Brought to the Station by a Gatekeeper

Chen Was Furious and Planned to File a Criminal Lawsuit

The dancing girl, Chen Hailun, when she went to the Paris Cinema to watch a movie last winter, was introduced by another dancing girl, Xue Meimei, to Xu Qizhong, the son of Xu Guannan, a prominent family in Wuxian. Xu saw Chen's beautiful appearance and was amazed by her. From then on, he followed her every day, and often went to Chen's residence at Nianwu Village, Fuxu Road, to invite Chen out, either to the cinema or to the dance hall, and was very intimate. On May 5th of this year, Chen and Xu, because of their close relationship, went to the law firm of Yan Luqing together to sign a cohabitation agreement, stating that if Xu terminated the agreement in the future, he would have to pay 30,000 yuan in alimony. Unexpectedly, on the afternoon of the third day of the previous month, Xu invited Chen to the Da Guangming to watch a movie as a pretext, and took the opportunity

to return home and took all of his belongings away. By the time Chen found out and went home, it was too late. After that, Xu disappeared. Therefore, Chen often went to Xu's house at No. 61, North Zhejiang Road, to demand that the contract be fulfilled, a total of six or seven times. However, Xu not only refused to fulfill the contract, but often greeted her with closed doors. Later, Xu sent a mediator to resolve the matter, but the amount discussed was too far apart and could not be resolved. Until the day before yesterday (the 24th), Chen, because this matter had been delayed for a long time and Xu still ignored it, and because Chen was facing financial difficulties and had pawned all her clothes and ornaments, had no choice but to go to Xu's house with her mother, He, and her grandmother, Zheng, that morning to ask for money. When Chen entered the door, she was immediately met by the gatekeeper, who was fierce and grabbed Chen's mother, beat her, and blew a whistle to summon Chinese and Western police officers, who brought Chen, her mother, and her grandmother to the police station. The police chief questioned the gatekeeper, and the gatekeeper admitted that his master had ordered him to beat them. After the police chief questioned them briefly, he dismissed them. Chen had no choice but to support her mother and hire a car to go home. Chen felt that Xu's actions were too deceptive and was determined to hire a lawyer to file a criminal injury lawsuit with the court.

So They Can Be Issued to Detained Prisoners

The Shanghai Second Special District Local Court Detention Center is now in autumn, and the weather is gradually getting colder. Most of the prisoners detained in the center have no clothes or quilts, which is very pitiful. Yesterday, they specifically sent a letter to the Xinwei Relief Society, earnestly requesting the allocation of 200 quilts. The letter said, "Respectfully, now that it is autumn, the weather at midnight is gradually getting colder. There are many prisoners detained in our center, and most of them have no clothes or quilts. Even those who are strong and healthy are prone to illness, let alone those who are weak? We have long admired your Society's benevolence and compassion, and earnestly request the allocation of 200 cotton quilts, so that they can be issued at any time. We are extremely grateful."

Three Robbers Who Plotted to Rob a Huge Sum of Money from the Bank of Communications Were Sentenced Separately 175

Shi Ruichang from Tongzhou conspired with Xu Fengqing, a local, and Hu Hanshan from Haimen. On the morning of August 14th, they colluded with Japanese ronin Nishi Eii and Hosotani Nara to rob a huge sum of money being transported by a certain traveler to the Bund branch of the Bank of Communications on Fuzhou Road. The plot failed, and Shi and others and the two Japanese were arrested by Chinese detectives Shi En and Wang Runhe of the Hongkou Police Station. A pistol and six bullets were found on the Japanese. The two Japanese were handed over to the Japanese Consulate for interrogation. Shi and the other three, together with Wu Songshan, the driver of the former Jiang Yuandong Motor Company, who was tied up in the Fifth District of the Chinese界, and the ropes and towels used to hijack the car, were handed over to the First Special District Local Court. After several investigations, a verdict was reached yesterday morning. Wu Zehan, presiding over the Third Criminal Court, announced the verdict. Defendant Shi Ruichang was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment, Hu Hanshan was sentenced to three years and six months, and Xu Fengqing was sentenced to three years. The number of days of detention before the judgment was finalized will be converted to one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. The exhibits will be confiscated.

A Young Woman Hanged Herself, or Was She Strangled by Her Husband? 177

The Court Autopsied and Determined that She Died by Hanging Herself, but Her Mother and Brother Insisted that She Was Strangled by Her Husband

The Landlord Stated that the Couple Often Argued

Wang Rongkun, the second son of Wang Fuda, the owner of Wang Taifeng Department Store at the intersection of Guangdong Road and Fujian Road, Changzhou native, is currently working in the insurance department of the British-owned Willie Yang Company, and is only 23 years old. In October of the year before last, he married the daughter Quanfeng of Fang Xushi, a fellow villager, through a matchmaker, and rented a pavilion room above the Xiangtaichang Clothing Store at No. 602, Dongyouheng Road. On the night of the 6th of this month, Quanfeng suddenly hanged herself. Rongkun reported it to the police station in charge, who carried the body to the autopsy room on Feilun Road. The next morning, they transferred it to the First Special District Local Court, and the prosecutor of Wancheng Hall and the forensic doctor went to the room to examine it. It was determined that she had committed suicide by hanging herself. An order was issued to the deceased's husband, Wang Rongkun, to sign a guarantee to claim the body and coffin for burial. Now, the deceased's mother, Fang Xushi, and brother, Fang Xianggen, have jointly hired a lawyer to file a criminal lawsuit against Wang Rongkun in the First Special Court, saying that Quanfeng did not hang herself, but was actually strangled to death, requesting that he be punished for murder under Article 284, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiao Xiefei opened a court hearing. The plaintiffs, Fang Xushi and her son, appeared in court and stated separately that about two weeks before Quanfeng's death, they suddenly received a letter from Rongkun saying that Quanfeng was critically ill, so Fang Xushi rushed over from her hometown. However, after arriving in Shanghai, she saw that Quanfeng was not sick, and that Rongkun should not have done this. However, the letter has now been lost. As for the incident, Xianggen did not arrive at the scene of the autopsy because he returned to his hometown to call his mother. Judge Xiao then said to the plaintiffs, "According to the autopsy by the prosecutor and forensic doctor, it was determined that she died by hanging herself, and only her left leg and foot had slight injuries. Now you claim in your lawsuit that there were fingernail marks on her neck and bruises on her waist, and that she was strangled to death. This judge has already asked the forensic doctor who performed the autopsy in detail, and they all said that they examined it very carefully at the time, and that there was no such phenomenon at all. Prosecutors, forensic doctors, and scribes are all civil servants, and their examinations are extremely accurate and fair. You only say that she was strangled to death, which is hardly credible. So, what evidence do you have?" The plaintiff, upon hearing this, still had no concrete answer, and only said that the second landlord had also witnessed it. Therefore, the second landlord, Luo Shurong, was summoned for questioning. According to his statement, "I am related to both parties in this case. The defendant Wang Rongkun and his wife moved into the pavilion room upstairs in April.

They often argue. On September 6th, at 7 p.m., Rongkun returned home and went upstairs, and a quarrel started immediately. I heard the man and woman cursing each other very loudly. There were no other sounds besides that. After a long time, it was silent. At 8:45 p.m., I heard the sound of the second landlord calling. I went upstairs and saw the deceased lying on the cement floor, her hands and feet were cold and she had no breath. I performed first aid. I started to find that there was a belt around her neck. At the knot, one end was four inches long and the other end was more than a foot long. Rongkun was squatting on the bed wearing pants. He got out of bed to untie the belt when he heard me speak. Four days before the incident, Rongkun kicked his wife in the butt because she was watching gambling 麻雀 and did not go upstairs." When questioned, the defendant Wang Rongkun testified, "I have been married to Quanfeng for three years and have never had a quarrel. Only on the night of September 2nd, I quarreled with her because she was watching gambling, but I did not kick her. I don't know how the injuries to her left leg and foot were caused. On September 6th, I returned to my apartment at 7 p.m. and had dinner at 8 p.m. There was no quarrel. Then I went to sleep. At 9:30 p.m., I woke up and my wife was not in bed. I turned on the light and saw that she was

lying on the ground. Because my hand has been ill for some time, I had no strength to support her, so I called out to the housemates, about five or six people, who all heard the sound and entered the room and lifted her onto the bed. I then saw that there was a silk belt around her neck. This belt originally belonged to me, but because I didn't wear it, I placed it on the bed, which caused her to take it and hang herself from the vertical top of the iron bed. Later, because the belt broke, she fell to the ground." The plaintiff's lawyer then requested that the coffin be reopened for re-examination and that the defendant be released on bail. The defendant's lawyer then requested that additional witnesses be summoned. The court then ordered the defendant to pay 500 yuan bail and rescheduled the hearing for the afternoon of October 6th.

Destroying a Brothel and Assaulting People: Pimps Showing Off Their Power 181

Bian Shou'an from Yangzhou, 49 years old, operates a brothel at 4 Shengji Lane, Chujia Bridge, in the French Concession, with five or six prostitutes. The business is quite prosperous. Chen Songfu, a young man from Changzhou residing at 85 Qianjiatang, French Concession, 20 years old, is a frequent patron of Bian's brothel. At 0:30 AM on the 24th, Chen and five friends went to prostitute Cai Bao's room at Bian's house to "have tea" (as they call sitting in a room). They played around for about an hour and left after paying four yuan. For unknown reasons, Chen and his companions became displeased. About five minutes after leaving, they returned to Bian's house, each armed with an iron ruler. Without inquiring, they assaulted everyone they encountered and destroyed everything in sight. When Bian came out to reason with them, he was beaten so severely that his head was broken, and blood flowed profusely. By the time the police arrived, the assailants had already fled. Only Chen was apprehended and taken to the Xiafei Road police station. After questioning by the police chief, Chen was ordered to be detained. The police also sent Bian to the hospital, where doctors bandaged him up before sending him home to recover. Yesterday afternoon, the police escorted Chen to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District. According to the police lawyer Yuan Jiahwang's statement of the case, he was charged under Article 294 of the Criminal Code. He also stated that the police still needed to investigate the case and arrest the accomplices at large, requesting that the defendant be temporarily detained and the matter investigated and questioned again at a later date. Following this, the victim, Bian Shou'an, recounted the experience of being assaulted. Judge Xiong Huicui verified the confession and ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody for another hearing on the 30th. He also ordered the victim to submit a medical examination certificate from the forensic office for verification.

Woman Commits Suicide Due to Hard Living Conditions 182

Zhang Cai, a woman from Yangzhou, 45 years old, and her husband Zhang Yunsheng, who works as a laborer on ships, lived together at 156 Rulianwan Road. However, Zhang's wages were very meager, leading to constant economic hardship. Because of this, Mrs. Zhang felt resentful after contemplating her situation the day before, and a pessimistic thought emerged. Alone in the bedroom, she found a rope and hanged herself from the beam. Later, her neighbor, Wang Shaodi, caught a glimpse of the scene and was horrified. She immediately called for several men, who managed to bring her down, but it was too late to save her. She had already died. After investigation by the police, they immediately reported to the Yulin Road police station, who dispatched detectives to investigate. The body was then taken to the Fielun Road mortuary. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo Wei from the First Special District Local Court arrived at the mortuary to examine the body. After taking a statement from Wang Shaodi, Mr. Guo pronounced that the deceased, Zhang Cai, had indeed died by hanging herself. The body was handed over to her husband, Zhang Yunsheng, who signed a guarantee to take it back for burial.

Robbers Arrested, Firearms Confiscated, Robbery Cases Investigated 183

Xu Yongyuan and Zhang Bingcheng, detectives from the Hongkou police station, arrested four robbers on the afternoon of the day before yesterday at Liulü Road Bridge, Wusong Road, and Xingjiazi Road in Zhabei: Ding Laowu, Xu Fuchang, Zhou Xingfu, and Wang Xiaoerzi, all from Jiangbei. Upon questioning, they learned that firearms were hidden at the home of Wang Huang, a woman living in a shack on Linping Road in Zhabei. The detectives then went to the fifth district, third branch office of the Public Security Bureau, accompanied by detectives, and arrested Wang at her address. They found a Mauser pistol and thirty bullets under the pillow on the bed. They took the suspects to the Public Security Bureau. Yesterday morning, Ding Laowu and others were escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District. Judge Wu Zehan presided over the hearing. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that the defendants had conspired with others on the morning of the 8th of this month to commit armed robbery at the Yitai Money Exchange at 997 Broadway Road, stealing 170 yuan in cash, which they divided and spent. Although Wang Xiaoerzi did not participate in this robbery, he was involved in another robbery on Jiaxing Road and should be detained. He requested that the court issue a writ to the Public Security Bureau to transfer Wang Huang for a joint trial. Defendant Ding Laowu confessed that he was invited to participate in the robbery by Zhou Xingfu, and that the pistol was held by a "small nose" (Zhang Xiaosanzi), who was still at large. He stated that the gun and bullets found at Wang Huang's house belonged to Ma Pi Zhao Jisheng. They used ninety yuan from the Broadway Road robbery to buy a pistol and thirty bullets, which were stored at Wang's house for future robberies. At the time of the robbery, "small nose" had taken the pistol with him. Xu Fuyou also confessed to participating in the robbery. Zhou and Fu stated that Zhang Xiaosanzi, who was at large, had initiated and invited them to participate in the robbery. Wang Xiaoerzi denied participating. Judge Wu ordered them to be remanded in custody for another hearing at a later date.

Update on the Land Defense Corps Platoon Leader Gun Murder Case in Lujing Township 186

Zhang Linqing, the platoon leader of the Lujing Township Land Defense Corps in Pudong, killed Wang Qinghua and injured several others. After being handed over to the court, Zhang Linqing was presented to the Local Court for interrogation. The defendant claimed to have been drunk after drinking two cups of wine, which led to the killings. The prosecutor pointed out that Wang Qinghua had died from gunshot wounds and that others, including Zhang A'gen and Zhang Xu, had been injured. Therefore, the case was not simply a matter of drunkenness. Yesterday, the prosecutor summoned his wife, Zhang Wang, to the court for questioning. First Lottery for Anhui Shexian-Yuling Road Bonds Held in Shanghai 189

The Zhejiang Province section of the Anhui Huizhou-Shexian to Hangzhou Highway has been completed to Yuling Pass. Anhui is completing the section from Yuling Pass to Shexian to connect with the Wutun Highway. The Anhui Provincial Government issued 500,000 yuan in public bonds, to be repaid by lottery over eight years, starting in September 1933, with a lottery every six months. The bond fund management committee has scheduled the first lottery for the bonds to be held at 3:00 PM on the 28th of this month at the Shanghai Banking Association. Invitations have been sent in advance to various organizations and hometown associations to attend and observe.

Mental Hospital Shows Success in Treating Mental Illness 190

The Shanghai Mental Hospital on Guling Road, Ren'an Lane in this city has, since its establishment, treated over forty male and female mental patients from this city, other provinces, and various medical districts of the First Special District Court. Some have recovered and been discharged after two weeks, while others have recovered after three weeks. The hospital's achievements are remarkable. Dr. Gu Wenjun, the director of the hospital, is a seventh-generation mental illness specialist from Chuansha with unique skills in treating mental illness in both men and women. He practiced medicine in Tianjin and Beijing for many years and enjoyed a great reputation. It is reported that Mrs. Jin Yu, residing at 5 Songyin Lane, West Granary Bridge in the city, had suffered from mental illness for seventeen years. She was admitted to the hospital on August 5th and discharged on the 24th of this month, completely cured. Another patient, Lin Yuying, residing at 75 Lane 13, Gaochang Temple, Riverside Road, had suffered from mental illness for seven years. She was admitted to the hospital on September 2nd and discharged on the 24th of this month, also completely cured. The hospital is dedicated to helping the world and does not charge poor patients for medical expenses, which is commendable.

A robbery occurred in Dengyun Lane. At around 8:30 AM yesterday, three robbers came to the residence of Zhu Zirong at 12 Dengyun Lane in the city. One was wearing a raincoat and a felt hat, another was dressed in coarse cloth clothes, and the remaining one was wearing a white spun silk shirt and pants. They tricked their way into opening the door under the pretext of asking questions. They drew a handgun, threatened and intimidated the Zhu family members, and confined them to a room. They then divided up and went into the rooms, searching through the chests and cabinets, stealing clothes, jewelry, and about a thousand yuan in cash, and fled with the loot. Afterwards, the victim submitted a list of stolen items to the Second District, Third Sub-station, requesting that they be pursued.

China Credit Reporting Agency Recruiting Investigators 191

The China Credit Reporting Agency has recently expanded its business and is establishing a branch office in Hankou, scheduled to open at the beginning of next month. Branch offices are also planned for Tianjin, Hong Kong, and other locations. Investigators are needed, and applications are now being accepted. The qualifications for applicants are as follows: (A) Qualifications: (1) Good health, proper appearance, clear pronunciation, and amiable temperament. (2) Age between 20 and 40. (3) Literacy and fluency in the local dialect; proficiency in English is preferred. (4) Commercial or investigative experience. (B) Compensation: Monthly salary from 30 to 80 yuan, with lunch provided. (C) Part-time positions: Those already employed who wish to take on investigative duties on a part-time basis are also welcome to discuss arrangements. Compensation will be negotiated separately. Those interested should submit a resume and a brief letter of recommendation to the agency at 4 Hong Kong Road. Qualified applicants will be invited for an interview. Unqualified applicants will not receive a response. All applications will be kept strictly confidential.

Ship and Wood Industry Union Holds Re-election Meeting 192

The Shanghai Ship and Wood Industry Vocational Union held its second re-election meeting yesterday in the auditorium of the City Party Headquarters. Over 120 representatives attended, with Hua Azeng, Lin Huang, and Chen Xiangquan serving as chairmen. After the reports were completed, Li Weilong, representing the City Party Headquarters, and Li Mengnan, representing the General Labor Union, oversaw the election. Ye Xianggao, Chen Binwu, Hua Azeng, Zhang Liqin, Lin Xuan, Lin Jingchu, Lin Cong, Liang Ming, and Chen Xiangquan were elected as directors. Wang Rongchang, Li Fusheng, Chen Posi, and Chen Zhang were elected as alternate directors. Cao Chengzong, Ruan Caibiao, Liang Wei, Xia Qiu, and Jiang Kang were elected as supervisors. Dong Ronghua, Lin Zhan Tiao, and Li Xifu were elected as alternate supervisors. They were immediately sworn into office. Following this, resolutions were passed: (1) to rent a new headquarters office, with expenses shared by the two branches; (2) to send another letter to the contracting parties of the trade association, urging them to strictly comply with the agreement to dismiss non-members to protect the livelihoods of members; (3) (omitted). The meeting then adjourned.

News of Election in the Shipping and Customs Brokerage Industry 193

At 3:00 PM on September 23rd, the Shipping and Customs Brokerage Association convened its first executive committee meeting, with representatives from the City Party Headquarters and the Chamber of Commerce in attendance. Those in attendance included Wang Yucheng representing the City Party Headquarters, Li Ruzhang representing the City Chamber of Commerce, and members of the association Shi Zhikun, Zhou Jingzhai, Zheng Renye, Xu Youren, You Senting, Tang Zhiqing, Zhu Xiechen, Wu Yaoting, Mao Yanling, Huang Yanfang, Chen Yiqin, Shi Ruzhou, Wei Yiqing, Chen Panjun, Zhu Hongyuan, Wang Boxin, and Li Mingsheng, totaling over twenty people. Wang Yucheng representing the City Party Headquarters led the oath of office ceremony. After the ceremony, the standing committee members were elected: Xu Youren received thirteen votes, Shi Zhikun received eleven votes, Zhou Jingzhai received ten votes, You Senting received eight votes, and Zhu Xiechen received seven votes. Shi Zhikun was immediately elected as chairman. The executive committee meeting was then held, resolving to reorganize the internal structure of the association. Zheng Renye was appointed as the supervisor of the accounting section, Chen Panjun as the supervisor of the education section, Mao Yanling as the supervisor of the public relations section, Shi Ruzhou as the supervisor of the investigation section, and Chen Yiqin as the supervisor of the general affairs section. The secretariat would be directly managed by the standing committee. Seven members were also elected to manage confidential documents: Shi Zhikun, Xu Youren, Zhou Jingzhai, You Senting, Zhu Xiechen, Zheng Renye, and Huang Yanfang were elected. Xu Youren and Zheng Renye were appointed to hold the keys to the safe. Xu Youren and Zheng Renye were also asked to jointly draft industry regulations with the secretariat for submission to the Social Affairs Bureau for approval and record-keeping. Regarding other matters, the committee felt the planned transportation by water and land could affect the industry, and the standing committee were directed to telegraph objections. At this point, the representatives began to leave, and the chairman adjourned the meeting.

Publishing World

Ren Wen Monthly, Volume 4, Issue 7. The "Ren Wen Monthly," which has been published for four years, has released Volume 4, Issue 7. Due to the large number of pages, publication was slightly delayed, but the content is more substantial than before. This issue includes "A Review of Colonial Issues" by Bai Jiao, which conducts a systematic study of the entire border issue. The material is carefully selected, and the arguments are insightful. The article provides a clear overview of the area, population, and resources of the border region. The analysis of the failures of past immigrantations is particularly insightful. "The Rise of Economic Nationalism" by Jian Bing is written by the famous German author Leqierte. His writings on currency and economics have been eagerly translated in various countries. This article describes the transformation of the world economy from international commodity exchange to economic nationalism, revealing the economic policies of various countries and the state of world economic warfare. "The 300th Anniversary of Ming Dynasty Official Xu Wending" by Xu Jingxian and Yan Su focuses on Xu Wending's diplomatic policies towards Japan, his views on the livelihood of the people, and his national defense plans. In our country, which is plagued by both internal and external troubles, this article offers valuable insights. "The 80 Years of Experience of Xiang Laoren" is a record of Li Denghui's introduction by Yan Huiqing during the founding of Fudan University, which is quite interesting. "Hua Xu Man Lu" by Wang Xiaoyin and "Notes of Mr. Qian Luxiang" both contain historical anecdotes and are interesting and humorous. "Reading Notes" by Wen Yu introduces "A Collection of National Crisis Opinions," which is essential reading during this time of national crisis. The magazine index includes 162 magazines and 7 daily newspaper supplements, with a total of 2,034 entries, providing an abundant resource. The annual subscription is 3 yuan, with an additional 1.8 yuan for postage for overseas subscriptions. The general distribution office is located at Ren Wen Monthly Publishing House, Nanchianjiatang, Lafayatte Road, Shanghai. All major bookstores in Shanghai and other cities are selling it.

Special Book on Dry Cell Batteries. The "Illustrated Experimental Manufacturing Method of Dry Cell Batteries" by Fan Fengyuan, published by the Living Bookstore on Tauffel Road in this city, is a brilliant and valuable book. The book illustrates the manufacturing process of dry cell batteries step by step with clear photographs. The components are listed in detail beside the pictures, making it very easy to understand. The text describes the chemical reactions and chemical formulas inside the dry cell battery, followed by a discussion of the polarization and local action within the battery, their drawbacks, and methods of prevention. Then, starting with Leclanche cells, the book details various manufacturing methods for dry cell batteries and also provides a detailed description of the method for making paste batteries, including the secret of using calcium, aluminum, and chromium powders to prepare the paste, ensuring that the reader thoroughly understands all the essential points and can conduct research. It also describes the components of the best batteries in various countries, some obtained from Germany and some through chemical analysis, all of which are closely guarded secrets of the manufacturers. The book also contains numerous experimental manufacturing reports, the causes of failures, and the author's excellent and accurate formulas for making dry cell batteries, as well as research papers, making it a comprehensive and informative resource. It is truly the world's only specialized book on dry cell battery manufacturing. The author guarantees the successful manufacture of batteries according to the book and promises to answer "all questions from readers about their attempts." Many contemporary celebrities have written inscriptions for the book, such as Cai Yuanpei and Ye Gongchuo, who wrote "The Secrets of Electrical Science," and chemists Wang Jiliang, Shen Xiongqing, and Zhao Yuheng, who wrote "Manufacturing Guidelines." Zhang Gongjiu and Zhong Zhaolin, electrical engineering professors at Jiaotong University, wrote "The Fruits of Research Shine Brightly." Radio expert Fang Ziwei called the book "A Resistance Tool," and battery expert Hu Guoguang stated that the book is indeed the result of years of painstaking research. Mr. Tian Xuwo Sheng stated that the book is so detailed that scholars can specialize in one field and achieve success. Yan Renguang of the Ministry of Transportation's Directorate General of Posts and Telegraphs said that even the photos alone enable scholars to understand the manufacturing process of dry cell batteries. The Jianhua brand dry cell batteries made by the author of this book are already selling well in Jiangsu, Hunan, Sichuan, and other places, with excellent results. The book is sold by the Shanghai Foch Road Jianhua Company, in addition to being distributed by the Living Bookstore. The Author's Bookstore on Four Ma Road and the Jianhua Company on Foch Road also sell the book. The price is 2 yuan per copy, plus 7 cents for postage.

Qiu Mugong's Illustrated English Card is Selling Well. Mr. Qiu created this card to make it easier for English learners to memorize and use English. The English words used in daily life are marked with pictures, each word is accompanied by a new-style phonetic transcription from the Oxford Dictionary and Chinese translation, so that learners can recognize words by looking at pictures, which is easy to learn and gives a definite impression on memory. The nouns of life, food, clothing, housing, transportation and entertainment are classified in detail for scholars to check at any time. All the new nouns that have not been included in the current dictionary, such as "red light," "anti-aircraft gun," "listening machine," and other words, are all included, which is more practical and is a convenient tool for learning English. It is published by Xiaoxing Bookstore on Qipan Street, Shanghai. Each box is 50 cents. Currently, a special discount of 20% off is offered. Purchasers from Shanghai and other places are extremely enthusiastic.

Qing Qing's Fourth Issue Innovates Content. The fourth issue of Qing Qing Bi-Monthly, Volume 1, was published the day before yesterday. The content and printing are more excellent than before. The pictures include the naming ceremony of the Five Aircraft, the Navies of the Five Great Powers, the Thugs of Imperialism, the Stormy Night in Shanghai, the technical performance of Flying General Sun Tonggang, Zhang Xueliang vacationing abroad, girls as mysterious as autumn, wood carvings, new film news, comics, human beauty, decorative beauty, Yungang Grottoes, and several scenes from the Mongolian Pilgrimage, the desert, and outside Yanmen Pass, which were obtained by Shen Yiqian on-site, introducing the unique mood of thousands of miles of desert to the Chinese people. This material is really rare and is the characteristic of this journal. In terms of text, there are "Singing Girl," "Lotus Pond Girl," "Love Story," "Shopkeeper's Daughter," and "Yi Ren," totaling more than 20,000 words, which are also delicate and touching. It is also reported that from the fifth issue, in response to readers' requests, several columns will be added, making calm and sharp criticisms and descriptions of political and social life, and making detailed and practical introductions and promotions on modern art and decorative beauty. The writers are all famous people in China, and contributions are welcome, which is good news for those who love to read Qing Qing. The publication of "Beauty and Hygiene Method" enhances life with beauty and hygiene as the basis. Dr. Ding Huikang compiled the "Beauty and Hygiene Method," from infants to adults, all the beauty techniques of posture, walking, appearance, clothing, hair, eyes, nose, lips, skin, muscles, breasts, abdomen, hands, feet, fingers and nails are explained in detail. There are also detailed remedies for congenital defects, such as strabismus, hare lip, facial scars, armpit odor, red nose, baldness, and anemia, which are all written in detail in the book. In addition, such things like facial massage, bathing and hydrotherapy, light and air therapy, which are closely related to beauty techniques, are described in detail at the end of the book. If scholars practice according to this, they will not only benefit from beauty, but their whole body will also be healthy. Hardcover volume, priced at 80 cents per copy. Printed and published by Medical Bookstore, 204 Mei Bai Ge Road.

Letter to the Editor 199

Dear Sir, I read your newspaper's report on the 25th of this month about a Central News Agency reporter visiting the Fisheries Administration Bureau of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Region. Director Yuan Jiaji now informs you as follows: 1. News item: After investigation, much of the content of this news item is untrue. Please correct it in the next day's newspaper to avoid confusion. Respectfully, Yuan Liangji, 9.25, addressed to the editorial department of Shen Bao.

Dear Sir, I have read your newspaper's September 2nd edition in the "Local News" column, which contains a news item about the Chonghaiqi Five Counties Association requesting a strict investigation of the remaining gang of thieves. The beginning of the article immediately implicates the Xin Renhe Wheel tragedy. The Yuxing Company's plot to kill peddlers is one matter, and the discovery of theft on the Jufeng Company's Baofeng Wheel by the Provincial Public Security Team on the water is another matter. One occurred before May, and the other was discovered within ten days. The facts are clear and cannot be confused. However, the association did not know about the theft beforehand and let it run rampant. After the Xin Renhe plot to kill five peddlers caused an uproar at home and abroad, they repeatedly and tirelessly added the theft cases that occurred afterward to the five peddlers who unjustly drowned at the bottom of the sea, so that their wronged souls in the afterlife still bear an unclean name. Our association is as concerned about the safety of passengers as you are about suppressing theft. We have already applied to the authorities to handle the matter strictly according to the law. However, for the sake of maintaining humanity, we will never allow the arbitrary framing of innocent people, so that timid and isolated travelers are given a bad name by those who plot to kill for money, which would allow the murderers to escape the law. Moreover, the victims are clearly five people, but the association suddenly claims four, as if another person on the Xin Renhe Wheel committed theft and drowned themselves, so that the company would not be responsible, and the defendants convicted by the court would not be subject to legal sanctions at all. In order to uphold justice and prevent confusion, this association hereby sends this letter, hoping that your newspaper will correct it. Furthermore, this case has lasted for five months, and the eighteen elderly and young victims are dressed in rags and live like beggars. As the weather is gradually getting colder, our association is unable to provide assistance beyond food and lodging. When the Xin Renhe resumed its voyages, the victims privately demanded clothing and food from the company. After being notified by the authorities, our association feared that there would be excesses, so we sent staff in a special car to stop them, waiting for a legal resolution. However, your newspaper's report on the disturbance when the Xin Renhe resumed its voyages stated that "upon careful observation, their appearance was no longer that of the plaintiffs who stood in court the other day," which is also untrue. We respectfully request that this be corrected as well, to clarify the truth and prevent expectations from being dashed. Sincerely, The Xin Renhe Steamboat Tragedy Relief Association, September 10, addressed to the chief editor of the Shen Bao.

Zhang Zhijiang Sends a Letter of Appointment to Tong Zhongyi to be a Judge for the National Examination 209

The 2nd National Martial Arts National Examination has been announced and will begin on October 20th in Beijing. Zhang Zhijiang, the director of the Central National Martial Arts Academy, sent a special letter yesterday to Mr. Tong Zhongyi, the director of the Shaolin sect of the Shanghai National Martial Arts Academy, inviting him to be a member of the judging committee for this National Examination. The original letter is transcribed below. I respectfully inform you that the National Government has approved the holding of the 2nd National Examination this year on October 20th. We have been diligently preparing and have sent letters to the provincial governments to recommend 30 people and to the municipal government to recommend 5 people. All the examination regulations and competition rules have been drafted and amended by the Preparatory Committee and submitted for promulgation. However, the athletes from each province and city are all outstanding talents of the time, and each comes with their own strengths, often appearing proud and different. Therefore, strict rules are necessary for the examination venue, and the judging must be fair in order to satisfy the feelings of the participants. I have long admired your enthusiasm for advocacy and your high reputation. I respectfully invite you, sir, to be a member of the judging committee for this National Examination, to measure talent with a fair yardstick, so that there will be no regrets about overlooked talents. I earnestly request your presence at that time to preside over everything. I am sincerely looking forward to it. Respectfully, Zhang Zhijiang, Director of the Central National Martial Arts Academy, addressed to Mr. Tong Liangchen.

US Leads in US-France Professional Tennis Match 215

Doubles Match Undecided Due to Rain, Another Singles Match Won by US Player

(Paris, September 24th, Havas) The professional tennis players of the United States and France held a doubles match today at the Roland Garros Tennis Stadium. The American team of Tilden and Pence won the first set 6-2. The French team of Cochet and Paraya won the second set 6-4. In the third set, the American team had a 4-1 lead, but a heavy rain suddenly came, making the court slippery, so it was stopped. The members of the competition committee decided to continue the unfinished doubles match tomorrow.

(Paris, September 25th, Havas) France and the United States continued to hold professional tennis matches. American player Spence defeated French player Paraya with scores of 2-6, 6-4, 6-3, 6-1.

Italian Bega creates new Italian 800m Record 216

Time of one minute and fifty point six seconds, close to world record

(Italy, Lorentz 25th Havas) Fifteen hundred meter world record holder Italian Bega ran the 800 meters today, breaking the Italian record with a time of one minute and fifty point six seconds, but not surpassing the world record. The world record of one minute and forty-nine point eight seconds was achieved by British competitor Hampson at the Los Angeles Olympics last year.

Lu Diping, Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, in order to promote sports among civil servants, ordered the formation of fitness clubs by civil servants of various agencies in the provincial capital and initiated three competitions: Lakeside Relay, Lakeside Walking Race, and Lakeside Cycling. (Moscow, September 24th, Havas) The People's Commissar for Education of the Soviet Union issued an order that all schools implementing general education in Moscow, Leningrad, and major centers across the country must make English and French compulsory subjects.

Teachers’ College Curriculum Discussion Meeting (4) 221

The Meeting Has Concluded

The teachers’ college curriculum discussion meeting convened by the Ministry of Education was held in the Ministry of Education from 8:00 AM to 12:30 PM on the 24th. The details have been reported in yesterday's newspaper. The details are recorded below. The attendees on the day included Qian Yonghe, Shi Renfu, Hu Shuyi, Zheng Xiaocang, Chen Jianbei, Gu Shusen, Wu Yan'yin, Peng Baichuan, Li Zhiou, Meng Xiancheng, (also representative of Wang Diancun), Jin Haiguan, Cao Chu, Dai Yingguan, Tang Changyan, Huang Zhifu, and more than ten others. Chaired by Gu Shusen, the five tables that had not yet been passed yesterday, (1) Number of Teaching Hours per Week for Each Subject in Teachers' Colleges, Table 2 (Applicable to Teachers' Colleges in Rural Areas), (2) Number of Teaching Hours per Week for Each Subject in Simple Teachers' Colleges, Table 1 (Applicable to General Simple Teachers' Colleges), (3) Number of Teaching Hours per Week for Mathematics in Simple Teachers' Colleges, Table 2 (Applicable to Simple Teachers' Colleges in Rural Areas), (4) Table of Number of Teaching Hours per Week for Each Subject in the Two-Year Kindergarten Normal Department, (5) Table of Number of Teaching Hours per Week for Each Subject in the Three-Year Kindergarten Normal Department, were discussed in detail and passed. In addition, three proposals were resolved: (1) Teachers' colleges should establish more subjects such as music, physical education, and fine arts to cultivate specialist teachers in these subjects, and when necessary, they may reduce or exempt students from studying certain required subjects such as arithmetic, physics, and chemistry. (2) Extracurricular group studies should allow students to freely choose based on their personality and interests. (3) The results of this meeting will be compiled by the Ministry of Education and distributed to the members of this meeting, and the members are requested to provide their opinions on the curriculum scope of each subject and submit them to the Ministry of Education for compilation and organization to serve as a reference for future curriculum drafting. As for the eight types of tables of the number of teaching hours per week for each subject in each semester of various types of teachers' colleges or departments passed at the continuous meetings, the content is very complex. Here is an excerpt of the total number of teaching hours per week for each subject in each academic year:

(1) Table 1 of Total Number of Teaching Hours per Week for Each Subject in Teachers' Colleges (hereinafter abbreviated where possible) Divided into three academic years, first academic year, both semesters, are 32 hours) Second academic year, both semesters are 32 hours, third academic year, first semester 32 hours, second semester 35 hours, (The prescribed average is calculated at 35 hours per week. If the average number listed above is less than 35 hours, the number of hours lacking may be used to study English and other elective subjects.

(2) Table 2 of Teachers' Colleges, both semesters of the first academic year are 35 hours, both semesters of the second academic year are 35 hours, first semester of the third academic year 36 hours, second semester 34 hours.

(3) Table 1 of Simple Teachers' Colleges, both semesters of the first academic year are 33 hours, both semesters of the second academic year are 34 hours, both semesters of the third academic year are 35 hours, first semester of the fourth year 34, second semester 35 hours.

(4) Table 2 of Simple Teachers' Colleges, both semesters of the first year are 37 hours, both semesters of the first year are 37 hours, first semester of the third year 35, second semester 33 hours, first semester of the fourth year 35, second semester 33 hours.

(5) Total Number of Teaching Hours per Week for Each Subject in the Two-Year Kindergarten Normal Department (hereinafter abbreviated), both semesters of the first and second years are 36 hours.

(6) Three-Year Kindergarten Normal Department, both semesters of the first year are 36 hours, first semester of the second year 34, second semester 36 hours, first semester of the third year 35, second semester 33 hours.

(7) Special Teachers' Department is divided into four groups: General, Physical Education, Art, and Labor. Each group graduates in one year with two semesters. The total number of teaching hours per week for each group is 36 hours.

(8) The total number of teaching hours per week for each semester of the One-Year Graduation Simple Teachers' Department is 36 hours.

The above teachers' colleges enroll junior high school graduates for three years of study. Simple teachers' colleges enroll elementary school graduates for four years of study. One-year and two-year kindergarten normal departments enroll junior high school graduates. Special teachers' departments enroll high school or vocational high school graduates for one year of study. Simple teachers' departments enroll junior high school graduates and provide one year of training to become teachers in simple elementary schools.

Local News

Regulations for Reviewing Student Status in Secondary Schools 222

Notice from the Municipal Education Bureau on Key Points

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued a notice yesterday to all secondary schools in the city stating that the regulations for reviewing the student status of new and transfer students admitted each semester by the schools have been revised and ordered to be followed since the last semester. As this semester has already begun, the previously issued regulations should still be followed. However, to further improve administrative efficiency, the following changes and points of attention are listed separately: (1) Except for transfer students in the second grade or above, whose credentials must be verified, the graduation certificates (or certificates of completion) of all first-year students in senior and junior high schools need not be verified. Instead, the documents can be directly submitted to the bureau for review to save time. (2) In the replies from various schools verifying credentials last semester, some used formal reports while others used letters, which made the review process cumbersome and prone to omissions. In the future, all replies should be submitted as formal reports to facilitate the review process. (3) The newly issued regulations for reviewing student status last semester stipulated that the credentials of transfer students from other locations should be sent directly to the original school's highest educational administrative organ for verification. However, some schools failed to comply strictly, directly sending inquiries to the students' original schools, which was not in accordance with the procedures. This should be strictly observed in the future, and the regulations should be followed to avoid errors. To facilitate the verification of credentials for transfer students from other locations, a separate list of the highest educational administrative organs in various provinces and cities is provided below for your attention. (4) All official documents for verifying credentials should clearly state the details, such as "Student 000, admitted to the 0th grade of senior or junior high school, 0th semester, in the 0th academic year of this school," to facilitate verification by the relevant authorities. (5) The last paragraph of Article 6 of the newly revised regulations for reviewing student status in the last semester stated that "For students transferring from other schools in this city, a student status form should be filled out and submitted to the bureau for record, and there is no need to fill out a student status card." Now, the student status form is being issued, and you are required to follow this procedure and submit it together with the graduation certificates of new students and the student status cards of new students and transfer students from other locations to the bureau before October 10th without delay. (6) All credentials that need to be verified must be sent out for verification no later than October 15th without any delay. You are required to comply with these instructions separately.

Attached is a list of the highest educational administrative organs in various provinces and cities:

(1) The following are provincial education departments: Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Guangdong, Guangxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, Fujian, Jiangxi, Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, Hebei, Shaanxi, Sichuan, Gansu, Xinjiang, Ningxia, Qinghai, Suiyuan, Chahar, Xikang. (2) The following are municipal social affairs bureaus: Nanjing, Beiping, Qingdao. (3) The following is the municipal government: Hankou. (4) The following is the Weihaiwei Administrative Office.

Introducing Xu Siyuan's New Book 224

"Human Nature and the Destiny of Man"

The philosophical writings of Chinese scholar Xu Siyuan have been circulating overseas and have long been highly regarded by prominent figures in the contemporary intellectual world. For example, the great philosopher Santayana said that the author possesses a special talent in inner analysis, and the great Eastern poet Tagore said that the author's writings have profound wisdom, enough to enlighten many readers to understand the true meaning of life. In recent years, the author has written a book based on his personal experiences of life, published in English, entitled On The Nature and Destiny of Man. According to the author's preface, the book's content draws heavily from the teachings of Western philosophers Plato, Kant, and Nietzsche, and remotely coincides with the doctrines of the Confucian school before the Qin Dynasty. After publication, first-class scholars abroad who read the book expressed great admiration, which is a rare honor in China's intellectual world. Excerpts from various reviews are translated below: (1) German writer Thomas Mann (Nobel Prize winner in 1929): "The publication of this book will surely make the author's intellectual genius noticed by the world." (2) German philosopher Driesch: "This book gave me great interest and inspiration. The author's analysis of the ethical theories of Kant and Schopenhauer is simply amazing. I agree with every point." (3) Austrian poet and writer Van Fowler: "From this book, I have come to know the philosophy of the soul, the philosophy of life, and especially the philosophy of the artist, which is by no means a set of dry and tasteless theories. In short, it is a philosophy that can melt the intellectual products of Europe over the past centuries with the ancient Eastern wisdom." (4) British Poet Laureate Masefield: "I read this book with great interest and admiration, and I am confident that this book will transmit the light of wisdom to millions of readers." (5) British playwright (president of the Drama Association) Bax: "I am largely sympathetic to the thoughts expressed in the solemn and quiet words of this book. In this era, it is truly heartening to find an author who is more concerned with the permanent problems of humanity than with the noisy disputes of politics and economics." (6) British biologist and philosopher (one of the founders of evolution) Morgan: "It is very pleasing and valuable to read this book in old age." (7) Irish poet Shaw: "Concise and clear, very sufficient to express the author's ideals." (8) French writer Gide: "Reading this book in the midst of illness, depression, and loneliness, my spirits were immediately refreshed." (9) American philosopher and writer Santayana: "This book is full of reason and elegant sentiments, enough to imagine the cultural origins of ancient countries. Even the concepts adopted by the author from the West, such as the concept of 'pure love,' seem to be able to blend with their own ideas without separation." It is heard that the sales agents for this book are Shanghai Kaiming Bookstore and Nanjing Zhongshan Bookstore.

The Jinan University Alumni Association Holds its Annual Meeting 225

The Shanghai Alumni Association of National Jinan University held its annual meeting yesterday at 11:00 a.m. at the Bankers' Association Clubhouse. President Zheng Hongnian, former director Huang, Dean Ren Zhiyu, Secretary-General Yang Yufen, and more than a hundred alumni attended. They dined together, making it a grand occasion. Wang Wei, Long Ziqiang, and Jiang Shanqing served as the presidium, and Wei Zhenhua took notes. Chairman Wang gave a moving opening speech. Then, President Zheng gave a speech, saying that he was very pleased to see that more and more alumni were graduating from the university and that the alumni association was becoming more organized. He hoped that they would continue to unite, help each other, serve the society, demonstrate academic spirit, and contribute their opinions to promote the development of the university with a passion for their alma mater. Former director Huang then gave a speech, saying that the association had an important mission and should set up a general manager to develop its affairs. Dean Yu and Secretary-General Yang also gave speeches. Sun Yue, Yu Shaowu, Liu Wangsu, Lin Qingchi, Ping Zuren, and other alumni gave speeches with great sincerity. Finally, the constitution was revised, and the committee members were re-elected. The elected executive committee members (in order of votes) were Liu Wangsu, Sun Yue, Yan Benwen, Wen Wenyao, Li Bangshuo, Lin Qingchi, Yu Shaowu, Wu Baogui, Liang Bingheng, Ping Zuren, and Rao Zhuhua, eleven in total. The elected supervisory committee members (in order of votes) were Wang Wei, Long Ziqiang, Wei Zhenhua, Chen Xiwu, Zeng Yifu, Jiang Shanqing, and Wang Shanlu, seven in total. The meeting concluded at 4:00 p.m. with joy and many gifts.

The gold market initially declined yesterday but eventually rebounded.
