Sudden Decline in Securities and Public Bonds 231

Northern Gangs Sell Short, Bulls Exit

Various Bonds Decline, The Later, the More Severe

Yesterday, the Chinese Securities Exchange market suddenly experienced a sharp decline due to the serious situation in North China and numerous rumors. Short sellers and bulls exited the market, creating a sudden sense of tension. During the morning opening, Northern gangs sold vigorously, mostly shorting distant contracts, while bulls exited recent contracts. Disbandment distant contracts declined by 85 cents, while recent salt tax contracts declined by only 25 cents. This was because there were many short sellers in salt tax, so they compensated when the price fell slightly. In the second session, numbers 21 and 46 were also sold off, but those covering short positions were also quite strong, showing a struggle to rebound. However, due to the large number of sellers, the price failed to stabilize and continued to decline by about 12 cents. During the afternoon opening, there was confirmation that the "96 Reorganization" rumor was false, causing a sudden decline of about half a yuan. The other variables showed no signs of recovery and continued to decline by 5 to 23 cents. At the closing, the decline had not subsided. The aforementioned varieties continued to decline by 23 cents, with the trend weakening the later it went. Unified tax fell by 35 cents, and the salt tax fell especially sharply, plummeting by 70 to 90 cents. It was rumored that the news from the front lines was bad, and the market participants were hesitant to buy, causing the decline to accelerate. The final result was a uniform decline, ranging from 40 cents to 1.60 yuan. Among them, the entire 6 fell the most, at 1.60 yuan, followed by the 96, falling by 1.30 yuan to 1.60 yuan, and the salt tax falling by 1.15 yuan to 1.55 yuan. There is only one day left for this month's futures, and the market price changes will undoubtedly be substantial. The total transaction volume was 18,446,000 yuan, including 6,000 yuan in spot goods and 6,230,000 yuan in combined futures for unified salt tax. Spring and Autumn

In the Metropolis 240

— Shen Yan

In the metropolis (of course, I am not just referring to Shanghai), the dense growth of the population is directly proportional to the collapse of the countryside. The black line on the statistical table always shows a significant rise every six months. However, what exactly are these countless people doing in the metropolis? I feel that it is more accurate to say that they are engaging in hand-to-hand combat rather than settling down and prospering. Therefore, those who intentionally want to occupy a considerable position in the metropolis and share some material enjoyment must have at least the following two skills:

(1) Lack of a Sense of Shame: In the metropolis, the most taboo thing is to be afraid of embarrassment, and the most suitable thing is to be thick-skinned. When necessary, you should not blush even after being slapped in the face. You must put on a smile, a very natural smile, not even a bitter smile. Whether this slap is received in front of one person or in front of a thousand people, as long as the person who gives you the slap can bring you considerable benefits, you must endure it. If you think there is a need for further contact, you may kneel down and recognize him as your godfather, regardless of whether he is older or younger than you. When you encounter a foreign master, after being slapped, although you cannot recognize him as your godfather, you must say a few words of "Yes, Sir!" This way, you can be invincible.

(2) Maximum Westernization: As long as the money in your pocket is willing to help, in the metropolis, the first thing you must do is wear Western-style clothes, and leather shoes are of course indispensable. Even if you don't have enough money, old Western-style clothes and old leather shoes are absolutely necessary. If you like to smoke, it is best to smoke a pipe. When speaking, you must include a foreign word in every three sentences, especially in public places. If you have the opportunity to make a couple of foreign friends (it doesn't have to be British or American, even Portuguese or Russian people are fine, and Japanese people are of course even better), don't miss it. You must spare no expense to curry favor with them. Once he is willing to walk with you on the street, then your face will be greatly enhanced! When walking, when taking a public bus or streetcar, and in the library, don't forget to bring a copy of a foreign newspaper or carry a Western book in the original version, even if you don't understand it. You must pretend to understand it and don't be afraid of your arms getting tired. In short, when a person is in the metropolis, the first priority is to imitate foreigners in everything, whether it is walking, eating, dressing, or going to the toilet... You must try to Westernize as much as possible and be thoroughly Westernized.

Friends, when you are in the metropolis, don't forget to study these two skills, otherwise you are incorrigible!

Achievements 241

— A Jie

Whether male or female, living in this world, it is nothing more than making some "achievements." Is inventing new principles and new things an achievement? No. Is establishing virtue, establishing words, and establishing merit achievements? No. Is making money, opening a store, and acquiring property achievements? No. What I say is the "achievement" of life, is the crystallization of love, (children).

The Flower Name Treasure Scroll says: "Thirty without children is mediocre, forty without children is lonely, fifty without children is not respected, sixty without children severs kinship. It is really bitter to be without children in old age, like Coptis chinensis, which is extremely bitter." This idea of ​​ancestral succession is deeply imprinted in the minds of our countrymen. In fact, it is all Mencius's fault. He said: "There are three unfilial acts, and having no offspring is the greatest." So today, three wives and four concubines are not uncommon, and rough manufacturing and declining products are common. If there were not this theory, our country's citizens would not be so numerous. The population would not be excessive, unemployment would naturally be reduced, and it would certainly not affect the country's governance. Therefore, to save China, the first step is to stop making "achievements." Speaking of personal suffering, the reason also lies in the indiscriminate making of "achievements." Sniveling Ah Da, scabby Ah Er, mangy Ah San... children surround the knees, and grandchildren fill the hall. People congratulate and say, "What a blessing!" In fact, there is "energy," but it is difficult to say "blessing." Poor people are especially good at finding poor fun and strive to create "achievements." Children cry and women wail, which is exceptionally lively. Living expenses, education expenses, medical expenses... make them complain endlessly. Is this not the retribution for finding too much poor fun?

In the current situation, it is difficult for gentry gentlemen to talk about enjoying the blessings of children, and friends from Jiangbei already know the burdens of children. Economic burdens are the inherent duty of the father, and there is no complaint. As for reputational burdens, we can only use the motto "One mother gives birth to nine children, and the mother has ten hearts" to defend ourselves. With anger in the belly, where can we seek redress? We can only regret that we did not find a proper way to have fun at the time, and we made such unlucky "achievements." It is also useless!

At the exhibition, "achievements" are not useless, especially when you, old man, return to heaven. Obituaries, coffins, and spirit curtains are important times and applications for "achievement" exhibitions. At other times, the effectiveness of "achievements" is very, very small. However, because you, old man, worked diligently during your lifetime, you earned a lot of inheritance. Then, your achievements, A, B, C, and D, will naturally fight each other at that time. Although you want to reach out from the coffin and slap your world brother twice, it will be too late!

The "Three" Principles 242

— Dao An

When officials swear in, there are three no-ism: no use of personal people, no waste of public funds, and no acceptance of bribes. There are often also three no-ism in military declarations and communiqués: the muzzle is directed outward and not inward, people do not offend me, I do not offend people, and enemies attack, and there is no resistance. Aunts also have three no-ism: they are not allowed to be close to their master and the big woman, they are not allowed to interfere with their physical freedom, and they are not allowed to hinder their romantic life.

Modern youths have three aesthetic principles: love beautiful girls, sensuous curvaceous beauty, and decorative beauty and goodness. Modern girls have three joys: to like lovers in suits and shoes, cars with electric wind, and colorful banknotes. General fashionable young grandmothers have three expenses: expenses for fashionable clothes and cosmetics, expenses for watching movies and playing mahjong, and alimony during divorce.

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 243

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 16: Heartbreak When Current, Still Blessings; Military Affairs When Hurry, Army Suddenly Transfers in Secret

When Gan Jizhi's hand pressed on the table, and he was looking outside, there happened to be a rickshaw puller from Haidian who was familiar with him, dragging his rickshaw past the shop entrance. Jizhi suddenly had an idea, immediately raised his head and called out to the outside, "Zhang San." Zhang San stopped and looked inside, saying, "Isn't this Second Master Gan? Where are you making a fortune?" Jizhi paid the bill for the wine and food, walked out, and said to him, "Zhang San, I want to go into the city, can you pull me for a ride?" Zhang San said, "Why not do business? Please get in the car." Jizhi said, "You haven't said how much you want." Zhang San said, "For Third Master's business, there's nothing wrong with saying it. Just send you to the city, and whatever money you give will be enough. I'll take it even if you give me a copper coin." Jizhi listened to him being so polite, so he had no choice but to get in the car without mentioning the price. Zhang San was a person who liked to talk, so he continued to pull the car, panting, and asked, "Second Master, I haven't seen you in a long time, are you making a fortune in the city?" Jizhi smiled and said, "I don't live in the city. And I can't talk about making a fortune." Zhang San said, "Don't you go to the Gan family's house in Haidian?" Jizhi said, "That's my brother's house, I don't go. Are the neighbors still the same as before?" Zhang San said, "There have been some changes. The Li family in the east, their old man died. Wu Laosan, who was next to you, has moved, and now a merchant lives there. The Yang family across from you is still very good. Now a company commander has moved in. Their old girl is now fashionable, and she also talks about freedom. She and that Company Commander Zhao are talking about free love. Haha!" Saying that, he burst out laughing. Jizhi's heart thumped a few times, he calmed down and asked, "What do you mean by free love? I don't understand." Zhang San said, "Don't make me laugh. You don't even understand the four words 'free love'. To put it bluntly, she will marry that Company Commander Zhao of her own accord." (197)

Modern 244

— Hua Ling

(Modern) Exactly what is "natural justice" is a little difficult to understand. Young ladies spend all day wrapped in clothes, hiding in boudoirs, keeping their delicate faces and slender hands "nourished snow-white," which is said to be "outdated." Women in the tropics spend the year naked and barefoot, except for the front and rear genitalia, without a thread, tanning their whole bodies black, which is said to be "unevolved." Only those who wrap themselves in coats in winter, hiding at home to heat the stove, and those who bare their arms and legs in summer are considered "modern." So, "modern" seems to have some meaning of "both outdated and barbaric."

Speaking only Chinese does not seem beautiful. Speaking only foreign languages seems to be in danger of being a foreign slave and not loving the motherland. If you can mix a sentence or two of foreign language, or mix three or five foreign words, between ten sentences of Chinese, then it is both beautiful and patriotic, and completely "modern." So "modern" seems to have the flavor of "impurity and confusion." Eating "Da Rao Mo" (large steamed buns) and "cornmeal" is for "Shandong villagers," who are only enough to use knives, sticks, sell explanations, and perform magic tricks on the street. Eating "wheat paste" and "wheat porridge" is for "stinky villagers," who are not presentable. But if you buy "oatmeal" or wheat-made "bread" from a catering company and eat it as food, there is no need to say that you are a rare "modern figure" among the yellow race. So "modern" seems to be interpreted as "blind following."

The union of men and women, requiring betrothal gifts and six rites, and formal marriage has been unanimously recognized as "pedantic." Without betrothal gifts and six rites, without matchmakers, men and women who love each other and live together, and who separate when they disagree, are also "vulgar," called "dating." If men and women love each other and practice "cohabitation" that is neither "dating" nor "formally married," that is the most "modern" way. So, "neither awkward nor awkward" seems to be considered "modern."

"Hanging," "swallowing match heads," "swallowing gold," and "taking raw opium" are all well known to be nineteenth-century "suicide policies." This kind of "taking tranquilizer pills" and "jumping into the Huangpu River" has not won people's support for a while. Only suicide by jumping out of a plane is considered a "modern" of autumn, 1933. So the definition of "modern" seems to be able to be said to be "cruel."

"Rare and bizarre" is considered "modern," and "unreasonable" is also "modern," but I finally couldn't find a "natural justice" of "modern."

Hunting Geese 245

— Cheng Zhaoxiang

The four of us crouched quietly in a small fisherman's hut on the beach of Donggang, waiting for the night tide of the fourteenth night of the lunar August. The waning moon rose at the end of the East China Sea, gray clouds stayed in the sky, the sea surged eastward, the waves roared, and the fine grass beach stretched out under the lonely fisherman's hut. Gan stood up, opened the small door facing the sea beach, looked at the sky, and then paced back impatiently and turned around on the yellow sand floor of the house. Min and Quan talked intermittently about hunting experiences. I sat alone by the door, the moonlight gradually shone into the house, and the sea seemed to have countless silver snakes dancing. We faintly saw distant sailboats as black dots. Everyone waited for the arrival of the tide to hunt the geese that floated in with the tide.

Temporarily forgetting the city's complex thoughts, coming to this lonely seaside is like being an aloof monk, and this light transcends another world! The light sea breeze blew through the reeds, rustling, and a refreshing feeling floated up to my heart.

When the water grass was submerged, leaving only the tops, we knew that the tide had arrived, and we got excited. The four of us divided into two teams. Gan and I were together, hiding under the eaves behind the fisherman's hut. Min and Quan, barefoot and carrying guns and ammunition, left the fisherman's hut and hid in a pile of reeds at the end of the shore, seventy or eighty steps away. Each of us agreed to use lip whistling as a signal. Whoever saw the geese first and was close enough to fire a shot would fire the shot first.

In fact, geese are the most united birds. As long as they hear even a little noise, they will fly away with a whistle! It is not easy to wait for them to come closer again. At first, only one sentry comes to the shore to scout. Only when they have scouted that there is nothing to harm them do they dare to call their kind to float in in groups, but it is rare for them to float close to the shore. The reason why we divided into two teams this time was also because we were afraid that they would not float in and we had prepared a gun hidden outside the shore!

Time passed minute by minute, but the geese did not appear. Gan and I became a little impatient. Crouching in the dark corner of the house, the heavy dew wet our hair, and there was a bit of coldness on our bodies. The tide hit the shore with a whoosh, but we didn't see half a goose. How anxious!

Suddenly, Gan's gaze noticed a large flock of geese flying over on the far sea! Several of them stayed down, but they were far from the shore and did not float in. Damn! At this time, our guns' range definitely could not shoot such distant geese. We had no choice but to endure it, endure it.

We hoped that they would float closer. I thought Min must have seen it, right?

At this moment, we were very anxious, afraid that they would just not come in, wouldn't that be terrible! Just as I was thinking, suddenly three more flew in with a chatter, about forty meters from the shore. Before they could settle down with a splash, there was a crisp sound from the reeds on the other side, reverberating crisply on the empty sea surface, and the echo returned and spread out again. The rest of the geese were suddenly startled and flapped their heavy wings, turned around and flew away, not allowing you any chance to fire more bullets. A wounded goose was spinning in circles on the water.

Gan and I cheered and ran over. Min sat in the reeds, unloading the bullet. Quan asked us, "Now that the goose has been shot, how are we going to get it ashore! The beach water is very deep, who will go down! What should we do?"

Finally, Min agreed to go down. He was not afraid of water. He could swim. It took him a lot of effort to get the goose ashore. Back in the fisherman's hut, we helped him dry his back, put on his night clothes, rested for a while, and left the lonely fisherman's hut. …………

Talking all the way, we were very happy, and the bright moon followed us above our heads. The wind quietly blew through the countryside, maple forest, and dew was cool on our hair and wet and heavy on our clothes. The autumn grass was without sound, without breath, soaked in dew.

The four of us, together with that goose, were on our way in the middle of the night of the fourteenth of August under the bright moon.

Free Talk

On "Female Students" 246

— Xu Qinwen

Currently, social news in newspapers often carries the term "female students." Calling those who study "students," and female students "female students," seems to present no problem. However, in the past, among the four classes of society—scholars, farmers, artisans, and merchants—only scholars engaged in studying. Therefore, once someone had studied, they could forever be called "students." In places where universal education is practiced, everyone has studied, so the term "student" is limited to those currently studying at school. Otherwise, it would be too broad, like the general term "person." Thus, "female student" should refer to women currently studying at school. However, the reality is different. Newspapers even refer to housewives who have never studied as "female students." A friend told me that his sister-in-law, who cannot recognize a single character, was also called a "female student" by the newspaper. Investigating the reason for this title, it is merely due to her short hair, leather shoes, and long socks. It is clear that this so-called "female student" simply means a young woman with modern attire.

It is said that the reporter who called her a "female student" certainly did not talk to her or inquire about her background. He merely glanced at her from a distance and then started writing the news. This is just one instance, but such cases are not limited to one. It generally reflects the current state of newspapers.

Originally, old women are "female students" of the past, and little girls are "female students" of the future. Simply using the three words "female student" is somewhat inappropriate. News reporters like to use this term, probably to cater to the general reader's psychology. Nowadays, so-called "female students" seem to have two strong legs, can play tennis and volleyball, and even swim in the water. They can sing with pursed lips and dance in fluttering cheongsams. Men who grew up in the environment of old moral teachings of abstinence are often somewhat lecherous. Seeing such "female students," they inevitably feel weak and entranced. However, to recognize someone as a "female student" simply because one sees short hair, leather shoes, and long socks is to be overly sensitive, showing a distance from the real "female students." The wife and mother are undoubtedly women with yellow faces and bound feet.

Reading "A Southern Journey" 247

— Xiaoxue

"A Southern Journey," in one volume, was written by Sun Jiagan (Yizhai) of Taiyuan, Qing Dynasty, and published by Zhang Mai. According to Zhang's postscript, this is "Duke Wending's most delightful work in his life," which was once "compiled into the 'Essays on Governing the World' by He Gong of Shanhua." However, the "Essays on Governing the World" almost halved the original text, so he feared that this article would be "incomplete." Therefore, he "rewrote and printed" it based on Duke Wending's original manuscript. It contains twenty-nine pages of main text and one page of postscript, with eleven lines per page and twenty-one characters per line. At the beginning, the author first explains his motivation for the southern journey: in the summer of Ji Hai, he took leave due to his mother's illness and returned home. In the autumn, he suffered the loss of his mother. He was unable to repay her boundless kindness, leaving him with lingering grief. Moreover, his wife suddenly passed away, and his young child died prematurely. Unable to sing and play music, he almost lost his sight. His studies met with misfortune, and he was trapped by his circumstances. He wanted to find a place to settle among the mountains and rivers, to avoid perpetual remembrance and sorrow. As the poem says: "I go out on a journey to express my sorrow; this is what it means."

Sun Jiagan's journey was entirely for sightseeing, "to express his sorrow." Therefore, the merit of this travelogue lies in its concise descriptions of scenery. On this southern journey, he passed through many places and traveled a long route. Starting from Beijing, he first toured Shandong. His description of Mount Tai is quite captivating. He writes:

Along the way, I craned my neck to look towards Mount Tai, but there was a light rain. Clouds and mountains were in disarray. Occasionally, I saw high peaks outside the clouds and thought they were it. Before I had traveled even a few miles, there was another taller one. In the afternoon, I saw a peak that was very high, with strange rocks jutting out, surrounded by mist and haze. I thought it must be it. Then the river channel opened to the east, and the mountain shape turned to the north. Looking from afar, there was an even taller one. It turned out that I was coming from the north of Mount Tai. In the morning, I saw its back; in the afternoon, I saw its arm. It was not until Taian Prefecture that I faced it directly. Moreover, it was covered by clouds, so I looked but did not see it.

After touring the important places in Shandong, he continued his journey to Jiangsu. He passed through Yangzhou, Zhenjiang, and visited Tianfang and Jinjiao Mountains, arriving in Suzhou, this earthly paradise. But what impression did he get? In his diary, he writes:

Suzhou controls three rivers, spans five lakes, and connects the sea inside and outside the gates. Goods are piled up like mountains, and people flow like water. The rows of shop signs are as brilliant as clouds and brocade. Speaking of its prosperity, it is not far from the capital. However, the customs are frivolous, and people boast and deceive. All artisans and commoners exhaust their wisdom and energy to create strange techniques and licentious crafts, which are said to be doing what is useless to harm what is useful.

Suzhou did not give him a good impression. So, after visiting the scenic spots of Taihu Lake, he "went south out of Wujiang and arrived between Jiuhang in eastern Zhejiang." He was satisfied with this area, and his impression was completely opposite to what he got in Suzhou.

The people are good at sericulture, and the land is planted with mulberry trees. Each household has a pond for raising fish, and each village has a canal for boats. Wheat and rice are lush, growing under the mulberry trees. Quiet girls carry baskets, and children dry nets. The scenery is clear and serene, different from the prosperity of the three Wu regions.

Why was he dissatisfied with Suzhou but felt satisfied in such an environment? It is easy to see in these two contrasting descriptions that it is due to the author's thoughts and his strong pastoral poetic sentiment. From there, he went to Hangzhou and enjoyed himself on the West Lake, then continued to Quzhou. I think the description of the scenery in this area is much better than the depiction of the life on the lake. He writes:

From Hangzhou, I went upstream along the Zhejiang River to Fuyang. The mountains of Fuyang are as majestic as the fortresses of Yan and Qin, but they are greener. South of Fuyang, the river channel gradually narrows, with two mountains facing each other, and a river flowing in the middle. The peaks are reflected upside down, and everything above and below is green. Leaving Tongzi Pass, the scenery gradually opens up. Mountains are arranged in the distance, all beautiful and charming. Mount Tongjun stands steeply on the riverbank, with a flat plain opening up to its south. The stone walls surround it like a natural city, which is Tonglu. Blocking the mountains and facing the water, the residents live among the mountains and rivers. The green tiles and white walls are spotless. Its clearness and brightness are fascinating.

After passing through Zhejiang, he went to Jiangxi, from Jiangxi to Hunan, and then to Guangdong. Later, he returned from Guangdong to Hunan and took the road to Henan towards Beijing. According to the author himself, this southern journey "covered three of the four seas, traveled through seven of the nine provinces, saw four of the five sacred mountains, and witnessed the entirety of the four great rivers." In an era when transportation was inconvenient, it can be said to be a grand tour. He said:

I left the capital in February, when the grass sprouts in Hebei had not yet grown. When I arrived in Wu, the flowers were blooming; when I arrived in Yue, the flowers had fallen. When I entered Chu, rice seedlings were being planted; when I arrived in Yue, rice was being eaten. Returning from western Yue, the autumn was old, and the sky was high. When I arrived in Henan, the leaves had all fallen, and when I returned to Shanxi, rain and snow covered the ground. In the blink of an eye, the four seasons circled around.

This travelogue is quite good at describing scenery. However, the argumentative parts of the article reveal a moralistic tone of conservative Confucianism everywhere, which is unpleasant. While on the boat and having nothing to do, I read this to pass the time. Writing this note under the lamp is truly a case of being idle and helpless.

On Autumn Creek 248

— Shi Fei

Where to find autumn? Only in the depths of the reeds on the clear creek... There, the footprints of autumn are always deeply engraved year after year.

On a certain night, the scenery on the creek is even more lovely... The wind is still, and the waves are calm, like glass that has just been wiped with velvet. The twinkling stars, the glistening moon, and the lines of flying geese imprint their shadows on the water. A gentle breeze blows, and the glassy surface wrinkles, turning into shimmering ripples. The reeds on both banks, wearing silvery-white flowers, sway in the wind, like a decrepit old man, standing alone in the vastness, nodding his white, disheveled head, appreciating the autumn colors. The half-dried reed leaves knock against each other, making a soft rustling sound, like the intimate whispers of lovers. At this time, a poet walks out of his ivory tower and strolls to this autumn creek. He intends to use inspiration to capture the scenery here and enrich his harvest of poetry.

He seizes the whispers of the reeds, locks in the ripples of the clear creek, cages the radiance of the stars and moon, and stops the flying geese in the long sky... placing them one by one into his poems. Thus, the poems, from the first line to the last, are filled with the sounds and moods of autumn. He thinks that the scenery on the autumn creek has all been captured in his net... Carefully holding his poems, he turns to leave, disdaining to glance at the creek again.

Suddenly, a single oar stroke is heard. The poet involuntarily looks back and sees a small boat rowing from the depths of the creek. The blue water laps against the hull, the cold moon shines on the oar, and the fisherman, who has just been awakened by the flying geese and is sitting on the bow, still has reed catkins clinging to his collar from the wind. "Nature" has arranged this creek into a picture of exquisite beauty, a poetic realm full of life. The poet stops in astonishment.

"It is not the poet who can be intoxicated by the autumn mood on the creek, but the sleepy-eyed fisherman; it is not the poems that can describe the autumn colors on the creek, but the elusive, wonderful hand of 'Nature'!" Thinking this way, the poet's poems fall from his hand, letting the clear wind blow them away, not regretting their scattered flight. At this moment, the poet feels for the first time a poetic feeling and autumn thoughts that cannot be written on paper.

Travel Jottings 249

— Tianma

Two, Ticket Inspection

Everyone of course knows what ticket inspection is, but ticket inspection on a ship is a little different, because every time there's a ticket inspection, it seems like a tragedy is being deliberately staged, making you unable to bear to watch it, but also unable to bear not to watch it.

This tragedy is staged as follows: a crew member leads a few deckhands, with a few armed but not majestic "comrades" following from a distance, searching for beasts like hunters, shouting as they walk: "Ticket inspection, ticket inspection!" Of course, the protagonists of this tragedy will definitely not be the gentlemen and ladies in the grand dining room, nor the compradors in the staterooms, and even the passengers in the mid-level cabins don't often get a role. The actors in this tragedy are mostly the poorly dressed, sallow-faced people in steerage, returning disappointed from the city or going to the city from the countryside with golden dreams.

The ticket inspectors shout louder and louder as they go from the grand dining room to the staterooms and then to the cabins. They know that they should use a certain tone and attitude when dealing with a certain class. Once they get to steerage, "Ticket inspection!" is no longer a shout, it's simply a furious roar. The deckhands and the "comrades" with special powers brace themselves, because experience tells them that there will definitely be many pitiful insects here for them to exert their power on, to tease, make fun of, and joke with. At this time, among this group of sallow-faced people, those who luckily have tickets of course cautiously take them out of their pockets, while those without tickets are flustered, heads down, silent, waiting for the inevitable misfortune to come.

"Tickets!" the deckhand shouts like thunder. "N-no..." a faint, murmuring reply.

"Pig, trying to sneak on board without a ticket. Go, to the purser's office!" Then a hero grabs the ragged collar like an eagle catching a chick and pushes him to the purser's office, and incidentally, you might even hear a crisp slap.

"Tickets!" he asks another person, a "retired comrade" wearing a gray hat or draped in a tattered gray coat. But what he takes out is not a ticket, but a "pass."

This is where our "armed comrades" get their turn. A "comrade" steps forward. "Why didn't you buy a ticket?" "I don't have money, I'm going home after being dismissed." The answer is also low. "To the purser's office!" The ending is usually the same. Like this, one, two, the purser's office is crowded with a large group – a group of prisoners quietly awaiting judgment.

Here, our purser and squad leader comrades should come on stage. As usual, they ask five at a time: "Why didn't you buy a ticket?" The answer is always the same: "I don't have money."

"Trying to sneak on board without money?" The purser sneers fiercely, and the squad leader shouts loudly. The group of poor wretches is always quiet, no one makes a sound.

"Search!" the purser orders. Several deckhands grab one, strip off his clothes, and search carefully, but the report is always that he has no money, or only a few coppers. (To be continued)

The students were all adults, almost all working at the open-hearth furnace construction site. They all understood what Dingga was saying at this moment. If someone were to run into the classroom at this time, they would never think that they were in a literacy eradication center class. They would definitely think that they were holding a meeting of the open-hearth furnace factory, like those being held everywhere on the construction site, discussing how to complete the construction of the factory within the deadline, so that the first open-hearth furnace could be put into operation on May 15th, and planning how to continue if possible... a gathering of the majority of people on many other issues. Maria Fotrovna was no longer a female teacher, no, she was just an attendee at the meeting, only able to speak in order of发言。. "This deadline cannot be said to be absolutely correct," someone said. "Yes," Maria Fotrovna said.

Casual Remarks

The Wonderful Opportunity of Lincoln 251

Today, I happened to flip through a foreign magazine, which contained an article titled "Lincoln's Opportunity to Become President." I found it quite interesting. His narrative is roughly as follows:

This famous president in history, Lincoln, had a son named Robert Lincoln. He was originally working as a clerk in Springfield, Illinois, and in 1859, he went east to apply to Harvard University. As a result, this brother's level was really too lacking. He failed fifteen out of sixteen subjects. His parents did not want him to return to Springfield, so they sent him to Phillips Academy for a year of remedial studies. There, his grades were quite satisfactory. However, Mr. Lincoln was afraid that his son would fail again, so he decided to go east to see him once for safety's sake.

At that time, their family's finances were not very good, so Mr. Lincoln had to give speeches everywhere to supplement his travel expenses. One of his speeches at the Cooper Union attracted the attention of the leading figures in New York City, who discovered his talent.

Initially, during the 1860 presidential election, William Seward seemed to be the most assured candidate. If Seward's plan of voting on Thursday afternoon had been followed, his victory would have undoubtedly belonged to Seward. However, because the printing house failed to deliver the ballots on time, it had to be changed to Friday morning. That very night, the forces of Lincoln and Cameron reached an agreement. As a result, Lincoln was elected president on Friday morning.

Later, Robert often said humorously to people that his father's election as president was really due to his efforts. If he had not failed so many subjects, his father would definitely not have gone east. If he had not gone east, he would never have been elected.

Indeed, this is true. If it were not for his son's failure that time, Lincoln might have quietly lived and died in his hometown. Who would have thought that his son's failure would have given him the opportunity to become president, to become a prominent figure in history? The world is so wonderfully unpredictable.

Therefore, I want to advise my beloved young compatriots, if you fail at something now, please do not be discouraged, because your failure may be the opportunity for your fathers, brothers, or yourselves to become great figures and achieve great things. However, conversely, if you encounter something very successful, please do not be overly arrogant and conceited, because your good fortune this time may also be the foundation for your fathers, brothers, or yourselves to be discredited and ruined in the future. The world is truly wonderful! Just like I happened to flip through this passage today, which made me turn over a thought, perhaps it also has something to do with my future destiny, so it cannot be said to be accidental!

A Clay Figure (Continuation) 252

Why are you crying so hard? Aren't the toys in the big box in the back room enough? What else do you want, you little brat!

The pockmarked nanny said at this time: "This was originally brought by Mr. Xi himself, the little master doesn't necessarily want anything..."

"Heh! Little thing, you didn't even see the person clearly!..."

In such a situation, asking "Is the master home?" would be too tactless. Old Xi had this kind of cleverness. Although he could not bear such a face, he had no choice but to endure it. He tiptoed out the door, returned home with a pale face, and could not help but grind his teeth and slam the table for a while, vowing never to go to "Xibao Xiaozhu" again.

However, (never go to "Xibao Xiaozhu" again) was just a statement made in anger. Old Xi could not give up that "considerable opportunity." His wife would never agree to him giving it up.

The wife thought that the next time they went to "Xibao Xiaozhu," they should first try to build a relationship with that "little fellow."

Unfortunately, Old Xi was so poor that he didn't even have money to buy something that could build a relationship with the "little fellow."

His daughter, Bobo, had a large clay figure, a "Wuxi Specialty," which her cousin who lived in Wuxi had sent her last year. Since Bobo didn't have "a big box of toys in the back room" like others, this "golden-headed, red-faced" clay figure had become her only beloved treasure. She dressed it up, put on a hat, and played with it all day long. It was Bobo's only good companion.

The wife's thoughts suddenly turned to Bobo's only companion: "Take Bobo's clay figure to coax that little fellow!"

"Hmm...?..." Old Xi could not agree with his wife's idea. He loved Bobo, just like all parents love their children....

"…………………"

"Hmm, that's the only way, I guess." Old Xi finally agreed with his wife's idea.

"………………" Bobo looked at her parents with wide eyes, hugging the clay figure, seeming to understand and not understand.

The wife winked at Old Xi, pouted, and started talking about something else.

When Bobo was asleep at night, the wife secretly took the clay figure, put it in a square box, and placed it aside.

The next day, Bobo discovered that her beloved clay figure had been stolen. Her cheeks turned red with anxiety. She asked her father, but her father said he didn't know. She asked her mother, but her mother said she hadn't seen it. Bobo cried sadly. The mother comforted her gently, and the father bought a penny's worth of candy to put in Bobo's mouth, and Bobo immediately stopped crying. The father put on his shirt, picked up the square box, and went out, saying that he was going to buy something good for Bobo. Bobo jumped up and down with joy. As Old Xi walked away from home, about ten steps away, he could still hear little Bobo happily shouting: "Come back soon, Daddy!"

The coolness of the ice cream calmed Old Xi's restless emotions. He stood up and walked back to "Xibao Xiaozhu."

He thought, surely that little fellow won't bother me again today? Surely that pockmarked woman won't say cold words again? ...Ah, such a beautiful and large "Wuxi Afu"... Bobo must still be crying!... No, if I get the job, I'll definitely buy ten of them for Bobo... Surely Lao Gu will have good news for me today...

Old Xi's heart was bursting with joy. He seemed to see Mrs. Gu's welcoming smile. He seemed to feel that he was already sitting in front of a mahogany desk. In an instant, Old Xi walked into the front door of Xibao Xiaozhu with extraordinary calmness.

The first thing he saw was the disheveled Bair dog and the nanny playing with their young master under the steps.

Old Xi walked quietly towards them. As usual, the child immediately stopped smiling and started crying.

"Mom! The fool is here again!"

The pockmarked woman pouted and looked away. The Bair dog also started barking wildly. However, Old Xi did not feel embarrassed today. He calmly opened the cardboard box, took out the golden-headed, red-faced "Afu" and held it high in the air: "Don't cry, good boy, I brought something good today!"

The child stared with his small eyes, and immediately smiled. He ran under Old Xi's arm and pulled on Old Xi's long gown.

"What? What? Give it to me! Give it to me!"

Old Xi smiled and handed the clay figure to the child. The child smiled, and the child's happiness made the dog and the nanny change their attitude. The child's happiness made Old Xi feel a burst of light in his heart.

The child held the clay figure and ran towards his mother inside, shouting loudly.

"Mom, a beautiful clay figure! Look!"

With a thud, somehow the child tripped. The clay figure was shattered, and pieces were embedded in the child's forehead. Blood flowed from the forehead, and the child wailed.

"What's going on? Why did you trip again?" The mother ran out from inside, flustered. "Hmm, Nanny! Who gave him this junk? How could he take this..."

Suddenly, a huge stone sank into Old Xi's heart, making him tremble all over.…………

The Different Ways the World Eats Dinner 253

How interesting it is to compare this question! However, I am not a culinary expert, nor am I a Western cuisine chef. Therefore, I may not be able to write about this issue completely; I will simply provide a brief report based on the detailed analysis of what I know!

Also, since the meals of various countries are comparatively richer and more complex at dinner, I will specifically use it to represent the others.

In the United States, during the prohibition era, no alcohol was available in restaurants or dining halls. Therefore, besides a large number of appetizers and fruits, one could only drink strong milk tea or coffee. However, in the restaurants opened by us Chinese, wine was surreptitiously served in teapots. As a result, Chinese restaurants were extremely popular among Americans at that time. But once the prohibition was lifted, they no longer needed to go to Chinese restaurants. As for the components of their meals, they mostly consisted of cheese, meat, protein, starch, and some pastries.

England is similar to the United States, except their dining rooms often do not serve alcohol.

Russia and Germany are generally the same. They have a bowl of soup and two or three plates of vegetables and meat. Italy, besides the soup, only has two types of meat, and very little at that. Even if you eat it all, you still won’t be full. However, their soup often contains a small amount of meat. Moreover, because they enjoy eating sour foods, they like to add vinegar to all three dishes. Pasta is also common. In addition, they eat rice once a week.

Spain and Portugal, besides a bowl of soup, have four kinds of meat, as well as ice cream and pastries, especially good cakes, and a lot of fruit. Hungarian soup contains meat, which is quite similar to our Chinese style. Norway, due to geographical reasons, often has no lunch. Dinner, on the other hand, features a table piled high with cold cuts and pastries, which guests can take as they please without any restrictions. The waiters only serve tea and coffee. Sweden, besides soup and appetizers, only has one dish of meat, but a lot of vegetables. If you don't like vegetables much, relying only on a bowl of soup and a dish of meat won't be enough to fill you up, but you can try some seafood.

Japan is a naturally frugal country, and there is no distinction between their dinner and lunch. Their rice portion is also very small. Usually, in addition to a small bowl of rice, the side dishes are only a piece of salted radish and a small plate of vegetables. Even middle-class families only add half a piece of raw fish. As for other meats, they are rarely seen except during grand banquets.

However, in our China, it is the complete opposite of Japan. For families above the middle class, the expenses for lunch and dinner are several yuan, tens of yuan, or even hundreds of yuan, which is not considered unusual. This expenditure is indeed astonishing.

Typically, dinners in various countries are usually between 7:00 PM and 8:00 PM. However, Spain often eats after 8:30 PM, and Germany at 7:00 PM.

Dinners are also not common [in Germany]. Because they have lunch at 3:00 PM, dinner has to be delayed accordingly. We Chinese eat at no fixed time. Young masters and concubines have breakfast at 11:00 AM or 12:00 PM, lunch becomes afternoon tea, and dinner is delayed until after 8:00 PM or 9:00 PM. By midnight, 1:00 AM or 2:00 AM, they still eat a midnight snack before going to bed. This is a common unhealthy habit of the upper class. We don't find it strange, but foreigners are always surprised when they see it!

Peng Xiang Deceived 254

Standing in front of the payment counter at ×× University, my hand trembled as I pulled out one hundred and thirty dollars from my waist. My heart ached. This was my father's hard-earned money!

After taking the receipt, I wanted to register. I couldn’t. I still needed twenty dollars for the uniform fee. I felt my pocket, and I only had fifteen dollars, but this was my book money. Heaven, what to do? Could I get an exemption? No. Could I pay later? I could, but if I registered tomorrow, I would have to pay a fine, two dollars a day!

There was no way around it. I had to pay the fee. I couldn't afford not to study. So, with tears in my eyes, I immediately went to my relatives in Shanghai to borrow the money. When I handed in those twenty dollars for the uniform fee, my hand trembled again.

Under the dim dormitory electric light, I wrote a letter home. After reporting this matter to my father, I said: This time, I was deceived.

War and Peace (3) (3) (Four-Act Play by Ling He) 256

Act III: Ode to Peace

Headmaster: Yes, this weather... Hahahaha! (The military authority appears on the balcony with the young master, followed by the wife.)

Wife: Well, since there are guests, why don't you go see them? Military authority: Ai! Why don't you understand this? This is the secret of us officials. (To the young master) Look! The red gourd on the roof, how red it is! It looks very good. Young master: That's right, it looks like a severed head.

Headmaster: Is Chairman Yu not here? Confidential secretary: No, he is here. But he is dealing with an extremely important matter. He will come out in a while.

Headmaster: Yes, yes, these days are the critical moment. He must be responsible to the country and the people, so... Confidential secretary: That's right, these days we are simply too busy.

Young master: Can you teach me to play cards now? Military authority: What are you saying? I'll teach you to play cards? And am I not very busy now? How can I have time to teach you to gamble?

Wife: I think you should play with him for a while; he is always bothering me all day long.

Headmaster: Recently, the armistice talks, I heard, are proceeding very smoothly, is that so? Military authority: Hmph, this is too much! This little child wants to learn to gamble. Go, pour me a glass of brandy inside. (Young master enters.)

Confidential secretary: How smooth can we say? But after many efforts from our side, now both sides are getting along very well. Especially the Japanese side has a fundamental understanding of us. This point can be gratifying to the people.

Headmaster: Being able to make the Japanese side understand is already a great achievement. But from my personal observation, I always think we should continue to resist. In terms of China's current position, we have only three paths to take in the face of this serious situation. One, direct negotiations; two, recovery of lost territories; three, resistance to the death. Now, the hatred of the general public towards Japan can be said to be unparalleled, so the current direct negotiations are extremely opposed by the people, which is undeniable... This is not to say that the government's handling of the armistice is inappropriate, but that the people are too indignant. As for recovering the lost territories, we are simply unprepared in terms of armaments and economy, so there is nothing to talk about. Confidential secretary: That's right, it is very true. Others have airplanes, tanks, and all kinds of sharp weapons. We have nothing. What do we rely on to recover the lost territories? Only those who have no military knowledge at all sing the high tune of recovering lost territories.

Military authority: (Drinks a glass of brandy from his son's hand. Looks at his watch again.) Hmph, I want a full ten minutes. Now I'll go see him. (Enters)

Modern Celebrities' Calligraphy and Paintings 257

Mr. Wang Wumin's Landscapes (Brief Biography) 258

Wang Nianci, style name Qiyi, also known as Wumin, is from Wuxian, Jiangsu. In his youth, he traveled as an official to Anhui Province. In 1911, he retired and lingered at Pingquan Study. He studied under Mr. Lu Lianfu of Wujiang, obtaining the essence of the Four Wangs. In the spring of 1924, he gathered over a hundred people to compile "A Grand View of Contemporary Famous Paintings." At the same time, there was "Wumin Studio Painting Album." Feng Gaosou, Zhu Jiangcun, Wu Changshuo, Pang Xuzhai, and others wrote more than fifty eulogies. Widely admired, his reputation is significant within the country. Now, tired of traveling in Yanshi and Taishan, he has returned to Shanghai. His works are increasingly known for their depth and simplicity, entering antiquity alone, cherishing ink and being self-admiring. Not many are in circulation.

Film Special

The Skills of Actors and the Director, Screenwriter, and One's Own Environment 259

— Bingyang

The issue of film actors' skills, as raised by Mr. Huang Junru in the 15th issue of this publication, is indeed an important matter. Because when making a film, if it is ignored, it becomes a newsreel.

It is good that Mr. Huang hopes that critics and audiences will pay attention to this issue. But beyond that, I think the most important key lies in the talent and experience of the director.

When shooting a film, the actor is directed by the director, which is a well-known fact. An ordinary actor, under the direction of a capable director, can show good results. Conversely, a talented actor under a mediocre director often buries his true colors. In the anecdotes of Hollywood's actor selection, we can find many such examples.

Secondly, many other conditions on the filming set can also affect the actor's skills. Take photography as an example. When an actor has not fully expressed a certain action (such as laughing loudly), a "Cut" suddenly comes from the director, and of course the result will definitely be unsatisfactory to the actor.

In addition to the relationship between the actor and the director as described above, there is also a necessary link between the actor and the screenwriter.

Under normal circumstances, if the screenwriter does not start from fantasy and tries to provide vivid facts, and if the screenwriter does not start from subjective imagination and can consciously understand the various realities of the actor, then this is of great assistance to the actor. On the contrary, if many unnecessary actions are made according to a dull script, the result is not only that the actor is criticized by critics and audiences, but also the director is helpless.

The third condition is also necessary, namely the actor's environment. The environment of Chinese actors need not be said. Let's talk about the Hollywood actors. Because the film business aims at pursuing profits, actors are ultimately not used as "people" but consumed as "machines." After a three- or five-year contract expires, you can get lost. Under these conditions, the actor's only hope is to shoot more films and get more money. Just imagine, under these circumstances, where do they have enough time to study the script, ponder the movements, and understand the psychology? Where do they have enough time to make great artistic in-depth studies? In the end, except for a few who sacrifice for art, I am afraid that most of them have only become the director's echo bugs.

I have put forward three opinions above in a scattered manner. My intention is not to ask critics and audiences to give actors some leniency for their skills. My intention is to point out that these conditions are very important before a film is made. Otherwise, it is unfair to criticize the actor based solely on the actor's performance, forgetting the other prerequisites that determine the actor's skills.

Film World Random Talks

Faith Baldwin's Advice 260

— Zhongqin

Faith Baldwin is an American art expert. The Hollywood Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences hired him as a judge and consultant. He spends his days in theaters. His criticisms of actors are always pertinent. The following are some mottos he wrote for actors.

Katherine Francis: You are one of the most affectionate women, especially in "The Playboy," but your dialogue is too forced. Be calmer, or a childlike attitude is most suitable for you.

Eddie Cantor: You are a major figure in the film world, but your laughter is an unnatural trembling sound. You have a great future, and I hope you pay attention to it.

Rock: Undoubtedly, your jokes are in the same category as Chaplin's, but Chaplin's works are full of infinite meaning, which seems to make him better than you. Please pay attention.

Chaplin: Your recent works are rare. I hope you will make a few more. Don't rely on hard work because you have become a rich man.

Gary Cooper: You drag out the syllables of your words too long. I know you haven't gotten rid of the Italian accent, please practice more.

Frederic March: You are just right in "The Royal Family of Broadway," but I hope you don't imitate Barrymore. He has his own style, and you can't learn it.

Katharine Hepburn: Your greatness in "A Bill of Divorcement" doesn't need my publicity, but I have also seen many of your stage plays. I think you can be a satirical actor, so I hope you don't play roles like "A Bill of Divorcement" again, and develop your satirical style.

Elissa Landi: You must never play glamorous roles. You are a quiet and gentle woman and should play quiet roles. You are also too honest.

Myrna Loy: You are very suitable for using compassion to make everyone sympathize. You can also insert humorous jokes in the middle.

Helen Hayes: Hollywood praises your beauty very much, but your acting is not entirely based on your appearance, which you should recognize.

ZaSu Pitts: You work too much, which has caused you to get sick. I am very worried about you. I hope you don't work on so many films in the future. You can focus your energy on one film. It is more energy-saving and easier to be refined than acting in many films. Mr. Stuart Hemsley said that you are a tragedian. I agree. If possible, try acting in a tragedy, but the public impression of you in comedies is too deep. Or you have to change your appearance, film after makeup, but I am afraid it will be very troublesome.

Clara Bow: You still have innocent enthusiasm. I hope you will use a young woman's enthusiasm to describe your unrestrained nature. You are older, which is needed, and you can't learn from naughty children anymore.

Bebe Daniels' Sentimental Words 261

— Luofen

British star Bebe Daniels once said to people: "If people in the film industry want to become famous, there is no other way but to go to Hollywood. London, Paris, Berlin, and Vienna are not enough. Anyone who has talent can only go to Hollywood to avoid burying their own talent."

What does Bebe Daniels mean by this? She is not praising Hollywood, nor is she flattering it because she has been reused by Americans in Hollywood. Her words are very sentimental. Let's talk about the environment she encountered before to understand.

Bebe Daniels grew up in Bristol, England. Her father was a lawyer. Bebe Daniels was always precocious since she was a child. After graduating from middle school, she entered a music school. Later, she entered the Royal Academy of Dramatic Art in London. After graduating, she acted in stage plays in London.

Bebe Daniels was very frustrated in the stage play world. So she looked for other opportunities. She saw that the film industry in London seemed worth a try, but when she got into the film industry, because she didn't have any reputation, the result was the same as on the stage. For a long time, she was still a very small, unknown actor. She saw that the film industry in England was too conservative, and newcomers had no opportunities. So she decided to leave England again to look for opportunities.

Bebe Daniels first went abroad to Paris, where she was as frustrated as she was in London. She left Paris and arrived in Berlin. In Berlin, she initially had no opportunity to enter the film industry. Later, she was admitted to Ufa, but because the salary was very small, she resigned soon after. Later, she arrived in Vienna, the capital of Austria, where she didn't have a smooth day. Finally, she returned to London. When she traveled to various countries, she heard a lot about the Hollywood film industry, so she decided to go to Hollywood to try her luck.

Sure enough, she became popular in Hollywood, fulfilling her wish. In Hollywood, she is now a top-tier foreign star. When she first arrived in Hollywood, she played the leading role in MGM's "Clear All Wires". She sighed about her previous encounters, which is why she had the sentimental words: "Only by going to Hollywood can you become famous."

Beauty Standards in the Film World 262

— Bing

When it comes to beauty, people in Europe and the United States generally divide it into two types. One type, with golden hair and fair skin, is called Blonde, and the other type, with brown-black hair, is called Brunette.

Many movie stars in Hollywood are nothing more than these two major standards. But these two types of standard beauties have had many fortunate and unfortunate changes. During the most prosperous era of the Hollywood film industry, the so-called blonde beauties occupied the most popular position in the film world. Later, women with brown hair became popular and seized the position of blonde women. About six years ago, all film companies, no matter which one, used brown-haired beauties as the standard for selecting stars. At that time, blonde women all asked beauticians to turn their golden hair into brown hair.

But recently, blonde hair has regained its advantage in the film world's standard of beauty. According to Paramount Pictures' report, in a new film, the actors used to shoot a nightclub dance scene had as many as fifty women who were blonde. Only about ten women had brown-black hair and skin.

According to the results of the investigation, in the past five years, blonde beauties and brown-haired women have always maintained a balanced position in the film world, with occasional ups and downs, but no significant changes. The reason is very simple, because the current makeup techniques are very sophisticated, which can allow blonde beauties and brown-haired women to change at will.

Jacques O'Keefe and His Mother on Stage 263

— Bing

Jacques O'Keefe, the famous hat-throwing friend of Paramount Pictures, is a man who refuses to be easily subdued. He often sulks at Paramount over his treatment, but because of his good voice and decent acting skills, he is highly regarded by the general staff at Paramount. Last time, when he was filming "College Humor" for Paramount, he was asked to compensate for a day's absence, and he immediately resigned. Later, the company softened its stance. Although Jacques likes to throw his hat around, he usually works hard for the company. This time, he is playing the lead in Paramount's new film "Too Much Harmony." Because they were missing an old woman for a supporting role, the company was in great difficulty. However, Jacques O'Keefe dragged his own mother out of his home and introduced her to play the part. Because she was playing Jacques' mother in the play, Paramount auditioned her and the results were excellent, so they officially hired her. As for her salary, because she is Jacques' mother, it couldn't be less than Jacques', so it was set according to Jacques' salary. In the film industry, there are siblings or couples co-starring in the same film, but as for a mother and son co-starring in a film, Jacques O'Keefe and his mother are the first of its kind.

Movie Novel

Mirror Flower Water Moon Three-Cornered Moon (2) 264

Elizabeth thought that a noisy place like Brooklyn was not suitable for a refined artist, but putting him on the top floor of the apartment, with the nude paintings in the room and the sea view outside the window, might be acceptable. Perhaps occasional unexpected luxuries and the comfort of a home could make him forget the ferocious landlady, the dirty cloths in the small restaurant, and the cockroaches in the kitchen. Elizabeth remembered the various torments and humiliations that Leonard had suffered in the past, and she felt sorry for him. She hoped that from now on, under her protective wings, he could fulfill his great ambitions.

The Limburger family was in a complete mess. It always was, but this time it was especially so. Mrs. Limburger was washing her hair in the bathroom of her own bedroom, with soap and hair everywhere. The gramophone was playing loudly. Douglas was practicing fencing with his bare hands in front of the dressing mirror. Kenneth was arguing with his lover on the phone. And the youngest brother, Eddie, still wearing last night's dinner suit, was rummaging through the suitcase, throwing things around, making a mess everywhere. Elizabeth looked at it from upstairs and sighed.

But Leonard's room was much calmer. The typewriter was already set up upstairs. Novel manuscripts were scattered all over the bed. Elizabeth stood at his door. Leonard looked at her, but she knew he didn't see her. What he saw was the plot of the next paragraph of his novel, a masterpiece of "raging storms and thunder." She wanted to sit in his room and watch him, but her past experience told her that the noise of others would cause subtle chemical reactions in his mind. The big children were making noise downstairs, and the gramophone was grinding in her ears, but the sound suddenly stopped. Elizabeth went downstairs to see what was going on. She saw Mrs. Limburger arranging her wet hair, and the children were all gathered around looking at a telegram. Mrs. Limburger muttered to herself, "What is margin money? The broker says we need to add more margin money?" Kenneth ignored her. He said, "Listen, the telegram says that if there is no reply by 2:30 this afternoon, your account will be closed on your behalf. Mother, what is going on?" Mrs. Limburger said calmly, "Even I don't know." Kenneth shouted again, "Another telegram, it says, 'We have not received your reply so far, your account has been sold.'" Mrs. Limburger said, "This is the last telegram." The children looked at each other, and asked in unison, "What is going on?" Mrs. Limburger hugged her big belly with both hands, and nodded solemnly, saying, "This means that from now on we have to find another way to make a living." Kenneth grabbed the telegram paper in his hand and said angrily to his mother, "Why didn't you ever mention it to us? Mother, is our family property really gone? Do we have any stocks left?" (To be continued)
